CHAPTER 1 - INTRODUCTION
1.1   Background
Afghanistan's ethnically diverse population of 25 million is coming together around the
goal of national unity, and exhibits grounds well support for economic and political
progress. There is no longer a transitional government installed by a Loya Jirga in 2002;
there has been a general election. Significant international efforts to reconstruct
Afghanistan are currently underway, led by the United States and other international
donors. Different infrastructural development programs have been established by
international financial institutions such as the World Bank (WB), the Asian Development
Bank (ADB) and the government of USA. Business infrastructure is improving rapidly. In
September 2002, Government of Afghanistan signed the Law on Domestic and Foreign
Private Investment in Afghanistan, which allows, 100% foreign ownership, full
transferability of profits outside the country, international dispute resolution mechanisms,
and stream-lined investment licensing procedures. The law encourages and supports
private domestic and foreign investors. Its aim was to foster economic recovery, expand
the labor market, advance national revival, improve the standard of living, and help in
Afghanistan's reconstruction process. Investment in an enterprise can be in the form of
cash, credit, goods, services or other forms, such as intellectual property, trademark and
copyright. Qualified domestic or foreign entities may engage in investment in all
commercial and manufacturing activities.
Since the approval of the investment law, over 5,700 investment licenses have been
approved. Afghanistan's Ministry of Commerce inaugurated the Afghan Investment
Support Agency (AISA) in September 2003, a "one-stop shop" for investors to receive
necessary documents and other information for establishing a business venture. The
Afghan government has considered privatization of state industry and the development
of oil, gas, and precious and semi-precious stones to attract foreign investors.
In view of the high demand for the allocation of industrial plots by entrepreneurs, AISA
has decided to develop an industrial park in the outskirts of the Jalalabad city. AISA
awarded the contract of consultancy services for "Environmental Assessment, Planning
Studies, Preliminary Design and Final Engineering Design of Two Industrial Parks" to
National Engineering Services Pakistan (NESPAK) (Pvt.) Ltd. This report "Environmental
Impact Assessment (EIA)" has been prepared as per Terms of Reference (TOR) at the
Preliminary Design stage of the Proposed Project.
1.2   Project Rationale
The soviet invasion and ensuing civil war destroyed much of the underdeveloped
Afghanistan's limited infrastructure, industries and disrupted normal patterns of
economic activity. Gross Domestic Product (GDP) has fallen substantially after 1981 and
revived to some extent in year 2004 but still country is facing acute unemployment, less
export, and bad economy due to industrial as well as agricultural less economic growth.
Currently, Afghanistan's import reaches to some US $5 billion against US $450 million of
export. About half of the import includes cooking oil, soft drinks, processed food,
construction materials, etc.
1~                                   l-



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
Afghanistan shares borders with six neighbors- Iran, Turkmenistan, Uzbekistan,
Tajikistan, China and Pakistan and is considered a "land bridge". For centuries
Afghanistan has been the hub connecting Asia, Europe, and the Middle East. Today,
Afghanistan is ideally situated to again function as a strategic gateway, serving
landlocked countries to the north and the Iranian and Pakistani seaports to the south.
For the Central Asian republics and Russian industrial centers of west Siberia,
Afghanistan is potentially is the shortest route to the open sea. For Pakistan,
Afghanistan offers a primary route for the trade with Central Asia.
One of the steps taken to boost the country's economic condition is to provide
employment opportunities, rehabilitation of thousands of families rendered homeless and
jobless due traumatic experience of long drawn war and to achieve self reliance to
minimize imports and to enhance exports is the setting up of Industrial Estates all over
Afghanistan .
AISA is responsible to develop the new industrial parks/estates to provide investors
access to the developed land to set up professionally managed industrial estates. These
modern parks offer investors the benefits of high-quality infrastructure as reliable power
supply in "build to suit" sites, strategically located in several key industrial areas.
Designed to accommodate small, medium and large-size firms, the parks help investors
to avoid costly title disputes, and to reduce risks and delays associated with land
acquisition zoning and permitting. Hisser-e-Shahi Industrial Park is one of those
industrial parks/estates planned by AISA to achieve the ultimate objectives of the
government's policy.
1.3   Location and Salient features of the project
Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park is located in Rodat District of Nangarhar province,
Afghanistan. It is situated on Torkham-Jalalabad road at about 25 Km from the city of
Jalalabad and located at a distance of 200 m from the main Torkham-Jalalabad
highway.
The proposed Project Area is about 202 ha. This piece of land is the property of Canal
Department of Nangarhar Province. The land has been transferred from Canal
Department to AISA for the proposed Project. Figure-1.1 shows the location of Hissar-e-
Shahi site. Figure-1.2 shows the proposed boundaries of Hissar-e-Shahi site i.e. 204
Ha, 201 Ha, 202 Ha. The proposed Project will be implemented within two Phases.
Under Phase -I, about 106 ha and under Phase-Il about 96 ha of land will be developed
for infrastructural developmental activities. Initially, it was planned to develop the whole
106 ha of Phase-I of the industrial park, but later on due to financial constraints it has
been decided by the World Bank to develop the industrial park in stages under the Bank
financial assistance.
The proposed industries that would be accommodated under the proposed project are
as follows:
. Light Engineering
* Food Processing
* Leather Garments
. Carpet Weaving (Cutting, Washing and Finishing)

EIA Report
1.4   Regulatory Requirements
Afghanistan's Environmental Protection Act has been recently approved by the
government which makes it mandatory to carryout the environmental assessment for the
development projects which may cause the damage to the environment. Similarly, World
Bank's OP 4.01 also requires an Environmental Assessment (EA) for the projects being
financed by the bank to ensure that the project is environmental friendly and sustainable.
1.5   Objectives of the Study
This Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) report has been prepared keeping in view
the TOR as provided by the Client. The objectives of the EIA study are be to identify the
possible negative environmental impacts of the project as presently envisaged and
propose the required mitigation measures to be implemented in order to avoid the
negative impacts. The main objectives of the study include:
. Water and air pollution, noise and related nuisance during the construction
periods.
* Biological and chemical pollution load resulting from future industrial activities on
Industrial Estates, including air emissions, liquid and solid wastes,
* Health risk and various nuisances associated with liquid and solid waste
disposal,
* Right of way for the facilities, networks (water and electricity) and their impacts
on present land use and activities.
. Preparation of a detailed Environmental Management & Monitoring Plan (EMMP)
for the adverse environmental and social impacts.
1.6   Scope of the Study
This EIA Study has been carried out at the master planning and preliminary design stage
of the project. In spite of the fact, that very limited details of the Project are available at
this stage, but efforts have been made to assess the impacts and to propose their
mitigation measures for project activities particularly related to construction and
operation stage. Although a part of the Industrial Park is being financed by the World
Bank, but this EIA covers the whole area of the industrial park (Phase-1 and 11).
However, the data/information which needs to be updated or require detailed studies at
detailed design or operation stage has been identified in change management plan in
Chapter 7. A mechanism has been provided to include the findings of those
data/information and studies in EIA report.
1.7   Approach Adopted for EIA Study
The Consultants carried out the EIA study of the proposed industrial park in a systematic
manner. This included collection of secondary data, maps and related literature, field
surveys for primary data collection, public consultation, and desk studies. These are
summarized below:
Reconnaissance of the project area: A preliminary reconnaissance of the Project area
was carried out in March, 2006. The purpose of this survey was to familiarize the EIA
team with the physical, biological and socio-economic environment of the project area
3                                  1-3



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                              AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
and study area and identify the critical areas of environmental and social concerns. In
this respect, consultation was also made with knowledgeable people.
Secondary Data Collection: Secondary data pertaining to meteorology, land use,
geology, flora and fauna, etc. was collected from the secondary sources. An effort was
also made to collect the available maps of the project area from AIMS.
Field surveys: Surveys were carried out from 7th to 30th June 2006 in order to
investigate physical, biological, and socio-economic conditions of the Project Area and
Study Area (see Chapter 4) and identifying resources falling within the proposed Project
Area. To collect the baseline information on physical, biological and social environments,
checklists were prepared covering the following parameters:
i).   Physical Environment
* Soils
* Land-use pattern of the area including agricultural crops, barren lands, and hilly
area.
* Buildings including residential, commercial and animal use for complete/ partial
relocation within the Project Area.
* Cultural properties like mosques, shrines, mazars, graveyards etc.
a Archaeological monuments and historical sites.
* Other private/public infrastructure like telephone poles, hand pumps, tube-wells.
. Drainage aspects of the Project Area.
* Water resources (availability of both surface and groundwater).
* Air pollution sources.
* Noise pollution sources.
In order to get the baseline information about the water and air quality as well as noise
levels, monitoring was carried out within the limits of Study Area.
*  ii).  Ecological Environment
* Forests and game reserves in the Study Area.
* Existing vegetation in the Study Area.
* Trees to be cut due to the project implementation
* Wet lands within the vicinity of the Project Area.
. Migratory species especially migrating birds.
. Endangered species both flora and fauna.
* Wildlife in the Project Area.
. Beneficial plants and animals in the Project Area
: Aquatic life including fish resources, etc.
iii).  Socio-Economic and Cultural Environment
Enlistment of villages falling in the Study Area along with demographic information.
Socio-economic profiles of villages settled in the Study Area. The following major
aspects were covered in the socio-economic baseline survey of the sample population
settled within and along the Project Area:
. Demographic characteristics
* Literacy status/ education
. Nature of business/occupation
1-4



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
. Livelihood/income
.Living standard of the population
. Access to credit
* Social Infrastructure available
. Gender issues
* Pressing needs of the people
* Community perception about the Project, etc.
Public Consultations: Besides consultation with knowledgeable people during
reconnaissance of the Project Area, consultation with local communities through scoping
sessions was extensively carried out during the field surveys. These included general
public residing along the Project Area and targeted stakeholders that are likely to be
affected directly by the implementation of the Project. The purpose of the consultation
meetings was to assess stakeholders' views on the existing condition of the Project
Area, concerns stemming from the impact of construction and operation activities, as
well as safety-related issues.
Meetings with Government and non-government Agencies/Organizations:
To shear the Project  information  and     to   get    concerns,   views,
apprehensions/perceptions of the government officials as well as non-government
organizations (NGO) about the proposed project, a number of meetings were held at
Jalalabad. The government institutions which were visited during field survey in June,
2006 include AISA, National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA), Canal
Department, Agriculture Department, District Administration Rodat, Urban Development
and Housing Directorate Eastern Zone Jalalabad and Ministry of Industries and Mines at
Jalalabad. The NGOs offices visited during this field visit included International Rescue
Committee (IRC), GTZ, etc. List of persons contacted, various offices visited and
document consulted is attached as Annexure-I.
Review of Similar Projects:
To assess the impacts related with the project activities both during construction and
operation stages, similar projects were reviewed including Bagrami Industrial Park,
Afghanistan, Sunder Industrial Estate, Pakistan and Gateway City Industrial Estate,
Thailand.
After collection of primary and secondary data, analysis was made to assess the impacts
of the Project's existing environment. The impact assessment methods used include
network method and impact matrix (for details see Chapter 5).
1.8   Structure of the Report
The report is structured as under:
Chapter 2 provides the country's environmental policy, legal and administrative
framework applicable to the project together with the World Bank safeguards and
Guidelines. Chapter 3 presents the description of the project including project
components, project activities causing negative impacts, design parameters, detail of
infrastructure facilities etc. Chapter 4 describes in detail the existing environmental and
social baseline conditions of the Project Area considering the physical, eiological and
social environments. Chapter 5 exhibits the impacts assessment at the design,
construction and operational stages of the proposed project along with their mitigation
1-5



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
measures in order to minimize the effect of negative impacts. Chapter 6 provides the
analysis of alternatives considered during the EIA study. Chapter 7 depicts
Environmental Management and Monitoring Plan (EMMP) along with proposed
institutional framework required for effective implementation and monitoring of EMMP.
Chapter 8 provides the socio-economic baseline conditions, stakeholders consultations
carried out during the course of the study, social impacts and their mitigation measures
and recommendations for the need of the broader Social Assessment study. Chapter 9
includes conclusions and recommendations.
1.9   EIA - Project Cycle
The proposed project has the following stages:
* Planning Studies/Preliminary Design
* Detailed Design
* Constricting Stage
. Operational Stage
These stages will form the project cycle. This EIA is being prepared at preliminary
design stage of the project and obviously it is expected that at other stages certain
technical changes along with changes in the administrative decisions may differ with the
proposals of the EIA. Secondly, in EMMP (Chapter 7.0) there are studies that have to
carry out at later stages. Therefore, this EIA will be updated as an when required.
However, it is recommended that changes at construction and operation stages shall
only be included in EMMP.

3                    CHAPTER 2 - POLICY, LEGAL, AND ADMINISTRATIVE FRAMEWORK
2.1   General
This Chapter provides an overview of the policy framework, national legislation and
World Bank environmental and social assessment guidelines that apply to the proposed
project. The project is expected to comply with all national legislations relating to the
U           environment in Afghanistan, and to obtain all the required regulatory clearances.
2.2   National Policy and Administrative Framework
*           The political turmoil in Afghanistan as a result of its 25 years of civil war and foreign
invasion including an era of almost lawlessness and frequently changing regimes has
made serious impacts on its legal and administrative framework. The present
I           Government is still trying to consolidate itself in a number of areas and provinces.
Organogram of Afghanistan central government is attached as Annexure-ll. The
*           constitution of Afghanistan has been recently redrafted under the present regime and the
I           process of legal and administrative consolidation and practice is taking its effect.
Consultant's team has carried out a study of the existing relevant legislation relevant to
environment and social as well as the prevailing administrative system in the Study
Area. A list of the various laws of Afghanistan is given as Annexure-l1l.
The most relevant of these laws are the Environmental Act which has been recently
approved by the Government of the Afghanistan and Land Acquisition Act of
d           Afghanistan, which has been reviewed in detail for the preparation of this EIA report.
2.2.1   Environmental Act
3           Environmental Act has been promulgated to give effect to article 15 of the Constitution of
Afghanistan and provided all the management issues relating to rehabilitation of the
environment, conservation and sustainable use of natural resources, living organisms
*           and non-living organisms. The law clarifies administrative roles at the national level and
I           coordination with provincial authorities. It spells out frameworks for managing natural
resources conservation and biodiversity, drinking water, pollution control and
environmental education.
As per this act, National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA) define, as an
independent institutional entity, is responsible for coordinating and monitoring
*           conservation and rehabilitation of the environment, and for implementing this act. NEPA
U           is also responsible for the issuance of Environmental Permits after review of
environmental assessment report of the projects. This law clearly defines the functions
and powers of the NEPA. Following is the structure of NEPA:
r                . Director General
. Deputy Executive
*  Committee for Environmental Coordination
II               . National Environmental Advisory Council
* Sub-National Environmental Advisory Councils
*                 EIA Board of Experts
NEPA is also responsible to assess the effectiveness of the implementation of the
environmental legislations and regulations to improve the sustainability of the use and
i                                              2-1
l



}Iissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
IEIA Report
management of natural resources and the effectiveness of measures for conservation
and rehabilitation of the environment. To achieve the functions and goals, NEPA will
actively coordinate and cooperate with Ministries, Provincial Councils, District and
Village Councils, public bodies and private sector on all issues related to sustainable use
of natural resources and conservation and rehabilitation of the environment. Similarly,
Afghanistan Environmental Protection Act empowers the NEPA to take legal action
against the non-compliance of environmental legislations and regulations and penalties
may be imposed from cancellation of license to six months imprisonment, or payments
of a cash fine equivalent to the damage caused or even both.
2.2.2   Land Acquisition Act
The political turmoil in Afghanistan as a result of its 25 years old civil war and foreign
invasion including an era of almost lawlessness and frequently changing regimes has
made serious impacts on its legal and administrative framework. No other particular and
consolidated land acquisition laws are available in Afghanistan except the Land
Acquisition Act. Most of the land in Afghanistan is owned by the Government and
remaining land which is even owned by private persons has no legal records. The land
acquisition will be carried out according to the land acquisition laws of Afghanistan.
Section-40 of the Constitution of Afghanistan contains relevant legal provisions for the
compulsory acquisition of land in the public welfare. As per the current practice,
compensation is to be provided based on the Government rates determined by the
legally constituted committee. In case a land and property is acquired the owner gets:
a The value of land,
a The value of residential houses and buildings (commercial, industrial, religious),
* The value of trees and orchards, and
. Other assets on land.
The Act also states that the person, who loses residential land, will receive a new plot of
land of same value. If they wish they can get a residence or house on Government
property in exchange under the proper procedures.
In normal practice in Afghanistan for acquisition of land, land for land or compensation
for land is made incase of verified owners of the land. No compensation for land and
structures is made in case of illegal settlers.
The LAA is limited to a cash compensation policy for the acquisition of land and built-up
property, and damage to other assets, such as crops, trees, and infrastructure. The LAA
does not consider the rehabilitation and resettlement of disrupted populations and the
restoration of their livelihoods. However, AISA has ensured to achieve the objectives of
the World Bank OP/BP 4.12 by providing the financial assistance to the illegal landless
affectees for their resettlement through negotiations making resettlement in compatible
with World Bank OP/BP 4.12.
Although for this specific project land to be acquired for the proposed Industrial Park
belongs to government. Therefore, it is anticipated that no issues should arise in
transferring the land from canal department to AISA.
* 2.2.3 Law on Private Investment in Afghanistan
Law on Private Investment in Afghanistan was latest amended in December, 2005. This
legislation has been adopted to encourage, support and protect private investments and
enterprises under Afghan constitution, article (10), based on market economy
2 -2



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
regulations and governing its related affairs. As per this law the administrative structure
for the policy making for investment is High Commission on Investment. For the
implementation and monitoring of this law, High Commission on Investment has formed
AISA. The High Commission is composed of:
.Minister of Commerce,
* Minister of Finance,
* Minister of Foreign Affairs,
* Minister of Economy,
. Minister of Mines and Industries,
. Minister of Agriculture, Animal husbandry and Food,
* President of Da Afghanistan Bank,
* Chief Executive Officer of AISA as a non-voting member, and
* Two representatives from the private sector as non-voting members (Appointed
annually by the Chamber of Commerce of Afghanistan for one-year term).
2.3   Guidelines for Environmental Impact Assessment in Afghanistan
Guidelines for EIA in Afghanistan was published in 2003 and 2nd revision was published
in 2004. The purpose of this document was to take the first step in developing a formal
EIA procedure in Afghanistan. This procedure will form the basis of an administrative
process which can be adopted by the Government of Afghanistan. These guidelines
provide clear guidance to those involved in the EIA process as to how to proceed with
the initial stage of project screening. Following are the major heads of these guidelines:
* Scoping in the EIA Process
* Guidance on Preparing Environmental Impact Studies and Environmental
Management Plans
* Administrative Procedures for Submission and Review of EIA Reports
* Guidance on Public Consultation in the EIA Process
* Environmental Monitoring for EIA Projects
. Auditing of EIA Studies
The development and implementation of these guidelines will depend primarily on
improving the capacity within the Government to be able to adequately manage the
process. By necessity these guidelines provide some overall information on the EIA
process both from a technical and administrative perspective. During the preparation of
this EIA report these guidelines were consulted.
2.4   World Bank Environmental Guidelines
It is a prerequisite of the World Bank that the Government seeking for financial
assistance from the Bank for the development projects should carry out EIA and prepare
environmental management and resettlement plans (OP 4.01). It is also required that the
environmental and resettlement related planning should meet the requirements of the
Bank's operational directives and policies.
The environmental and resettlement regulations and guidelines of the World Bank have
been spelled out in the World Bank Operational Manual comprising documents relating
to Operational Policies (OP) and Bank Procedures (BP). These were originally issued in
the form of Operational Manual Statements (OMS), majority of which were later, after
2- - 3
1                                  2-3



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
updating, issued as Operational Directives (OD). Now these have further been updated
and issued as Operational Policies/Procedures. However, where Operational Policies
have not so far been issued, reference has been made to ODs.
Operational Policies (OP) 4.01
Besides identifying the general policy of the World Bank about the EIA, this document
lays down the procedures and guidelines for conducting EIA of the projects including the
aspects to be considered in EIA, public consultation and information disclosure
procedures. It also provides environmental screening guidelines for classifying the
projects into various categories (A, B, C and Fl).
Operational Policies (OP) 4.01 Annex A
This document provides definitions of terms that are frequently referred to in an EA, as
these appear in the Bank's perception and policies.
Operational Policies (OP) 4.01 Annex B
This document provides guidelines for the preparation of EIA report for Category "A"
projects (i.e. projects with significant adverse environmental impacts).
Operational Policies (OP) 4.01 Annex C
This document provides procedures and policies for preparation of (EMMP), including
aspects like mitigation measures, monitoring requirements and institutional capacity
building and training.
Operational Policies (OP/BP) 4.12
This OP sets policies relating to involuntary resettlement of population disrupted by the
project. Priority of the Bank's policy is to avoid displacement of the population. However,
if it is unavoidable it should be kept to a minimal. For that matter Bank provides
guidelines for considering alternative alignments of the project and making modifications
in the design. This document also provides guidelines for conducting census surveys,
preparing Resettlement Plan (RP) and reporting procedures.
The major guidelines are given as below:
* Involuntary resettlement should be avoided (where feasible) or minimized
* If relocation needs to be carried out, the displaced persons shall be consulted
and should have opportunities to participate in planning and implementing
resettlement programs.
* The policy also emphasis the identification of direct economic and social impacts.
* Preparation of a Resettlement Plan or Resettlement Policy Framework
Besides these OPs and ODs, the Bank has produced three volumes of Environmental
Assessment Sourcebook in 1991. which have been updated lately. The sourcebook
provides detailed discussion on Bank's policies, procedures, cross-Sectoral issues, and
Sectoral guidelines for the preparation of EIA.
2.5   Analysis of Bank's Safeguards
The following World Bank's Safeguards have been triggered out for the Project based on
the field investigations related to environment as well as social sectors.
-2-4



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
Operational Policies (OP) 4.01
OP 4.01 identifies the general policy of the World Bank about the EIA, lays down the
procedures and guidelines for conducting EIA of the projects including the aspects to be
considered in EIA, public consultation and information disclosure procedures. Annex B
of the policy provides the contents of EIA and Annex C exhibits objectives and contents
of EMMP, Capacity Development and Training, etc. As the Project is being financed by
World Bank, so EIA will follow the guidelines developed in OP 4.01.
Operational Policies (OP/BP) 4.12
This policy deals the issues and concerns related with proposed Project and provide the
guidelines to mitigate the adverse impacts on the local community particularly their
relocation. As 21 houses will have to be relocated, so compensation and relocation of
the affectees will be accordance with the guidelines laid down in OP 4.12.
2.6   National Environmental Quality Standards (NEQS)
Since Afghanistan does not have any standards for water, wastewater, air and noise.
Therefore, keeping in view the similar conditions, Pakistan National Environmental
Quality Standards (NEQS) has been taken for reference purposes. NEQS were first
promulgated in 1993 and have been amended in 1995 and 2000. In case no Pakistan
NEQS are available such as in case of ambient air quality, drinking water and water for
agriculture purposes, then the other standards applicable has been specified in the
report with justification.
The following standards are specified therein:
. Maximum allowable concentrations of pollutants (32 parameters) in municipal
and liquid industrial effluents discharged to inland waters, sewage treatment
facilities, and the sea (three separate sets of numbers)
* Maximum allowable concentrations of pollutants (16 parameters) in gaseous
emissions from the industrial sources
. For power plants operating on oil and coal
. Maximum allowable emission of sulfur dioxide
. Maximum allowable increment in concentration of sulfur dioxide in ambient air
* Maximum allowable concentration of pollutants (2 parameters) in gaseous
emissions from vehicle exhaust and noise emission from vehicles.
Pakistan's NEQS are attached as Annexure-IV.
2.7   Interaction with Other Agencies
AISA is responsible for ensuring that the project complies with the laws and regulations
controlling the environmental concerns of the construction and operation of proposed
Industrial Park, and that all pre-construction requisites, such as permits and clearances
are met. This section describes the nature of the relationship between the AISA and the
concerned line departments.
2.7.1   Federal and Provincial EPAs
AISA will be responsible for providing the complete environmental documentation
required by NEPA-Afghanistan and provincial NEPA Office at Jalalabad and remain
committed to the approved project design. AISA will be responsible to submit the reports
I                                   2-5



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
to NEPA for NOC/Permit. No deviation is permitted during the project implementation
without the prior and explicit permission of the concerned NEPA.
2.7.2   Ministry of Urban Development and Housing
AISA will coordinate to get approval for the plan from Ministry of Urban Development
and Housing prior to start of the Project construction activities. For this purpose AISA is
being coordinating with Ministry of Urban Development and Housing on day to day
basis.
2.7.3   District Administration
As the proposed Industrial Park is falling in the jurisdiction of Rodat District, AISA is
responsible to coordinate with district administration. In this regard, AISA has conducted
several meetings with the district administration and has committed to continue the
coordination in future.
2.7.4 Municipality of Jalalabad
to make the arrangements for solid waste management, AISA will also coordinate with
Municipality of Jalalabad to sort out the solution of the matter.

CHAPTER 3 - PROJECT DESCRIPTION
This Chapter provides an overview of the proposed Project including implementation
plan, proposed infrastructural development works, public facilities and provisions made
in preliminary design for environment, health and safety hazards.
3.1   General
The Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park is proposed over an area of 202 ha, located at about
25 km from Jalalabad City on north side of Torkham-Jalalabad Highway. The Project is
situated in Rodat District of Provincial Nangarhar of Afghanistan. The area can be
categorized as hilly terrain with gradual slope and few undulations over the proposed
site. Keeping in view the natural topography, the master plan and road network has been
planned to minimize the cut and fill. The land of the Project Area was owned by the
Canal Department of Nangarhar Province and now has been transferred to the AISA.
The proposed Project has been divided into two phases depending upon the financial
arrangements by the AISA. Under Phase -I, about 106 ha and Phase-Il about 96 ha will
be undertaken by the Project for development purposes.
3.2   Implementation Plan of the Project
The proposed Project will be implemented in the following stages:
* Design Stage
* Construction of Infrastructural Development Works Stage
* Construction of Industrial Units and Operation and Maintenance Stage
i).   Design Stage
Design stage of the project proceeds with the preparation of Conceptual Plans (Master
Plan) and Preliminary Engineering Design following the Detailed Design Stage. The
current project description is based on Master Plan and Preliminary Engineering Design.
ii).  Construction Stage
During construction stage, physical construction of infrastructural development works
like road network, storm water drainage, water supply, waste treatment plants, etc. will
be carried out through private contractor(s). It is expected that the project will be
awarded through International Contract Bidding (ICB). However, it will be decided at
detailed design stage of the Project.
iii).  Operation Stage
Initially, just after construction stage, construction of private industrial units will be carried
out by the5 private investors and already developed infrastructure will be operated and
maintained by the AISA. However, when all the industrial units will be constructed, 0 &
M of the Project will be shifted to the "Manager" (an organization controlled by the
private investors, for details see Chapter-7).
3-1



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.3   Salient Features of the Master Plan
The Master Plan of Hissar-e-Shahi industrial park has been developed considering the
actual requirements for the development of industrial park and future growth potential as
well as infrastructure requirements. It aims at fulfillment of spatial requirements of the
users and Client's aims and objectives in accordance with international standards of
industrial planning & infrastructure development. Draft Master Plan of the site is attached
as Figure-3.1. The main project features along with detail of amenities are given below:
3.3.1   Development of Land Use Plan
The proposed development plan has been bifurcated into two phases, Phase - I & II,
extending over 106.6 & 96 acres respectively. A breakdown of land uses suggested in
the Hissar-e-Shahi industrial park is given in the Table 3.1. The land use plan primarily
consists of industrial area, commercial area, roads & streets, parks & playgrounds as
well as public uses & utilities. As evident from the following Table, industrial area is the
biggest user of the land spreading around 64% of the industrial park area.
Table 3-1: Land Use Distribution Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park
Sr.      Land Uses        Phase-      Area ( Ha)    Total     Percentage
1      Industrial Area      59          70.8       129.8        64.1
2     Commercial Area       3.6          0.0          3.6        1.8
3      Roads/ Streets      29.5         21.8        51.3         25.3
4   Parks/ Play Grounds     2.5          0.7         3.2         16 --
3  5   Public Uses/ Utilities  12          2.7        14.7          7.2
106.6        96.0        202.6       100.0
3.3.2   Zoning of Industries
The Hissar-e-Shahi industrial park is envisaged to house four different types of
industries which include:
* Light engineering
* Food processing
* Leather garments
* Carpet Weaving (cutting, washing and finishing)
It is believed that all of the industries suggested in the park are quite similar in terms of
processes involved & compatibility.
3.3.3   Phasing
As already mentioned, the Hissar-e-Shahi industrial park is to be developed in two
phases. Initially, Phase - I will be developed with infrastructure development options 1,
2, 3 & 4 (refer Master Plan of Hissar-e-Shahi). These options have been developed on
the basis of discussions with AISA and World Bank team held in September/October
2006, based on availability of development funds for the project. The options are
essentially a strategy to achieve the full level of infrastructure development in increments
as and when the funds are made available to the sponsors.

3.4   Typical Industrial Processes
As referred above, the proposed industries of the Project have been divided into four
main groups and typical industrial units and their process within each group has been
briefly described as under:
3.4.1   Light Engineering
3.4.1.1 Aluminum Doors
Aluminum doors will be manufactured from pre-formed or extruded aluminum profiles.
Door making operation includes cutting of profiles, drilling, screwing, etc. Rubber and
other fitting materials will also be used.
3.4.1.2 Furniture Products
Seasoned wood of different sizes and varying shapes will be used for furniture making.
Wood will sawed to required size, planned and then fitting of pieces takes place. For
fitting of pieces, mostly synthetic glue is used in addition to wood or metal fasteners.
Assembled furniture will be then polished using spirit based varnishes or synthetic
paints.
3.4.1.3 Cooking Wares
Cooking wares are generally manufactured by forming of sheet metal (aluminum and
stainless steel). Forming processes will be carried out manually or by using of hydraulic
presses. Before forming, the sheet, is cut to the desired size and shape. After forming
the product, it will be polished using mechanical polishers.
3.4.1.4 Plastic Industry
Various plastic products will be manufactured from plastic resins, sheets, tubes, profiles,
etc. The plastic material used will be PVC, PE, PP, Polystyrene, Melamine, etc. Pipes
will be manufactured from compounded plastic resins using extrusion process. Dishes
3-3



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                              AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
are formed by thermo-forming of compounded plastic resin. Number of other products
will also be formed by cutting of plastic materials.
3.4.1.5 Spare Parts
Fasteners (nuts & bolts) will be manufactured from metal rods or plates, using punching,
lathes, presses, and shaper machines. The material used can be steel, stainless steel
and brass.
3.4.1.6 Locks
Locks will be manufactured from metal rods and plates, using punching, lathes, presses,
shaper machines, etc. The metal used can be steel, stainless steel and brass.
3.4.1.7 Tiles
The principle raw materials for the ceramic tiles are clay, silica and feldspar. Other raw
materials include wide variety of minerals, pigments and synthetic compounds used to
manufacturing of diverse products.
The raw materials are crushed and ground to the desired size fraction of each material.
The following forming processes are used:
. Extrusion.
* Soft plastic forming.
* Dry Pressing.
Thermal treatment is an essential step in the manufacturing of ceramic tiles. Thermal
treatment includes drying, firing and costing. A tunnel kiln is the most prevalent
equipment for thermal treatment. A periodic kiln is ordinarily used for small-scale
production.
3.4.1.8 Light Agriculture Tools
Light agriculture tools are manufactured by machinery and pressing of steel
sheets/plates or cast materials. After forming the tools are tempered in a furnace.
3.4.2   Food Processing
3.4.2.1 Salt Processing
Common or table salt will be manufactured by crushing and grinding of rock salt.
Additives are added to impart free-flowing properties to salt.
3.4.2.2 Fruit Juice
Fruit Juice or Nectar operation covers fruit like: apples, apricots, peaches, plums and
grapes. The steps in processing include receiving, storage, washing, extraction of Juice,
finishing, juice concentration and packing/bottling.
3.4.2.3 Biscuit Process
Biscuits are prepared from flour, as main raw material, mixed with other ingredients. All
materials are purchased as finely ground. The main ingredients are mixed with little of
water, butter or oil and then pressed into the desired shapes. Raw biscuits are then
baked in a tray or tunnel ovens at specified temperature and duration. Finished biscuit
are then packed.
3-4



FIlissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.4.2.4 Spices
Spices are mostly ground products of dried spice materials. The raw dried material is
ground to desired specifications and then packed. All grinding and packing is carried out
under controlled atmosphere.
3.4.2.5 Cooking Oil
Raw cooking oil is obtained mostly from oilseed crops. At first stage, the oil is extracted
by mechanical means. Further extraction is carried out using solvents. Free acidity in
crude oil is neutralized with caustic soda to produce soap as by-product. Oil is bleached,
deodorized and packed. During purification, steam is required. The meal or oilseed cake
is sold as cattle feed. Filter cake with negligible quantities of oil is disposed off. The
solid materials are readily amenable to separation from water and disposal.
3.4.2.6 Beverages
Beverages include mineral water and aerated drinks like Coca Cola and Pepsi. Mineral
water is produced by the treatment and sterilization of spring or high quality ground
water. Other aerated beverages are produced by controlled dilution of proprietary
concentrate. For dilution of concentrate, purified water is used. The process is basically
bottling of drinks. Packing used are bio-degradable plastic or recyclable glass bottles.
3.4.2.7 Processed Meat
Meat processing plants are those whose operations are confined to dressing and curing
of carcasses for preparing specialty and other products, following slaughter of the
animals. The raw input generally consists of carcasses of cows and sheep. Processing
operations may be carried out in conjunction with a slaughter house or at a separate
location.
A rendering plant is one which converts the inedible and discarded remains of the
animals (such as fats, bones, heads, blood, and offal) into useful by-products such as
fat, oils and pertinacious solids. Rendering may be done on-site as an adjunct to
processing operations or off-site as an independent operation.
Meat processing produces a number of products which may be generally grouped as
follows:
. Meat cuts and related products (such as steaks, chops, roasts and hamburgers)
for hotels, restaurants and private consumers;
a Comminuted meat products, requiring substantial size reduction and mixing. The
final product will be in a casing or container, such as sausages or sausage meat.
3.4.3   Leather Garments
Leather garments covered under this report are:
* Suitcases, Shoes and High Quality Ladies Bags;
* Handicrafts;
* Upholstery Industries.
Garment industry uses tanned leather as primary raw material. Other materials used are
threads, button, zips, and various linings or attachments. Processes involved are
trimming, cutting, stitching, finishing and packing.
3-5



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.4.4   Carpet Weaving
Carpets after weaving are subjected to trimming (cutting), washing and finishing.
Washing process involves use of detergents.
3.5   Preliminary Engineering Design
The preliminary engineering design of various infrastructure services has been carried
out and is described in detail as under:
3.5.1   Leveling and Grading
Leveling and grading will be carried out in two stages, i.e. (a) leveling and grading for
roads and (b) leveling and grading for development of zones.
The alignment of roads has been kept to follow the existing gradients so as to avoid
excessive cut and fill. The leveling and grading is planned within the proposed right of
way (ROW) to construct the road network and to properly lay the various utilities.
Excavation will, however, be required to attain the grade level for the proposed R.O.W.
and width of roads with permissible cross-slopes. Some re-routing of the existing nullah
will be required to facilitate the construction of culverts and re-shaping of the area for
use as planned. Generally the roads will be kept 20 cm above the existing ground in
relatively plain areas to protect from sheet flow generating from the adjacent land.
3.5.2   Road Network
Road network has been proposed to provide access to various industrial units and
related facilities. Road network shall consist of two types of roads with R.O.W of 50 m
and 30 m. The ROW of 50 m and 30 m has been proposed to accommodate road width,
walkways, median strip and services corridor for various types of roads. The design
speed of the road will be 30 km/hr within the Project Area.
The road width is dependent on number of lanes provided for each road. Road having
30 m ROW will have 7.3 m wide road (2 lane) each way with 2.4 m wide median,
whereas road having 50 m ROW will have 11.0 m wide road (3 lane) each way with 5 m
wide median and a cross slope of 2% will be provided for all roads to provide proper
drainage of the road surface.
3.5.3   Pavement Design
The pavement structure of roads will be designed as flexible pavement based on Corps
of Engineer's Method of Pavement Design. The design wheel load will be 12000 lbs. The
proposed flexible pavement shall consist of the following:
* Compacted Sub-grade
* Sub-base course
* Base course
* Wearing course
3.5.4  Traffic Sign and Marking
Informative and necessary traffic signs shall be fixed at appropriate locations. To
indicate the direction of typical traffic flow, road marking will be provided wherever
required.
3-6



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.5.5   Water Supply System
Tube Wells
To meet the daily water requirement of Phase-I (i.e. 0.52 MGD) it is estimated that at
least three tube wells of capacity 1.0 cfs shall be installed. It is anticipated that each
tube-well shall operate for eight hours daily. Similarly to meet the water requirement of
Phase-l1 (0.58 MGD), same number and capacity of tube wells shall be required.
Water Storage
Water obtained from the tube wells will be stored in covered RCC under ground tanks,
from where it will be pumped to the overhead water tank of capacity 125,000 gallons
(Phase-l-Low Pressure Zone). However, water to high pressure zone shall be supplied
through the underground water tank. It is proposed in the preliminary design study that the
capacity of the underground tank will be based on one third of day demand, which will be
about 500,000 gallons including fire water dead storage of 120,000 gallons.
Pump Station
To meet the water requirement of Phase-I (low pressure zone), water from the
underground storage tank shall be pumped to overhead tank. For this purpose, pumps
shall be installed in the pump room, which is proposed to be constructed on the
underground storage tank. Three turbine pumps, two duty and one standby, each of 500
gpm capacity shall be installed. The duty pumps shall operate about 7 to 8 hours daily,
alternatively.
Pipe Network
A gravity flow water distribution network comprising of pipes, gate valves, air valves,
washouts etc. will be provided. The system will be connected to the overhead tower and
underground tank respectively for low and high pressure zones. The pipe network will be
connected to the industrial units and other facilities, through tee-off service connections
of the required size ranging from 25 mm to 75 mm diameter, depending on commercial
and industrial units requirement. A minimum pressure of 15m head at all levels will be
maintained.
3.5.6   Electric Power Supply
The industrial park covers an area of 202 hectares and it is estimated at initial stage that
for this park at fully developed stage a power plant of 105 MW will be required. The
proposal dropped as it was quite expensive. Therefore, it has been proposed that a 220 kV
transmission line which is coming from  Uzbekistan to Kabul with scheduled
commissioning of 220 kV grid station at Kabul in 2007-2008. will be extended to
Jalalabad where a grid station will be provided to meet the power requirement of the
proposed industrial park. However, initially a 10 MW power plant may be setup with
generating sets of 1.25 MW each. The grid station will be located well within the area in
possession of AISA, so no land acquisition is envisaged for erection of the facility.
However. exact location of the grid station will be decided at detailed design stage.
3-7



flissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.6   Provisions for Environment, Health and Safety Hazards
At preliminary design stage of the Project, proper consideration has been made to
propose the required infrastructure to minimize the environment, heath and safety
hazards. The following provisions have been made in this regard:
3.6.1  Waste Water Treatment Plant
A gravity wastewater collection and disposal system will be planned and designed for
this project. The system will comprise a network of pipes laid in the ROW of roads.
Wastewater from the industrial units and commercial areas will be collected by pipe and
manholes and disposed off into Central Wastewater Treatment Plant (CWTP) of capacity
0.6 MGD (Phase-I and 11). It is suggested that two separate units of plants for Phase-I
and Phase-Il to be constructed at the same location. Main treatment processes will be
comprised of four stages, i.e. Pre-treatment, Primary treatment, Secondary treatment,
post-treatment. The treated water will be used for watering of plantation and green area
and area to be acquired for future extension of the industrial park (for details see
Chapter -5). The CWTP is located within the land owned by AISA therefore no land
acquisition is required.
3.6.2       Storm Water Drainage
The storm water drainage will be planned keeping in view the topography of the project
site. Drains will be provided in the median along the roads to collect the storm water
runoff. All the organic wastewater generated within the industrial park shall be collected
through sewers and taken to the treatment plant. Only storm water will be disposed off
through drains. Box culvert will be provided at roads and streets for cross drainage.
During the rainy season storm water that would be finally disposed off through open
drainage system (as proposed above) may contain certain types of pollutants such as
grit, suspended solids, oil, grease, etc. These pollutants could exist on the outside paved
areas of industrial units, surface of primary and secondary road network, and open
unpaved areas.
It is recommended to provide retention pond within the industrial park project boundary
those would be integrated with the proposed storm water drainage system. The primary
objective of these ponds is to provide primary treatment to the polluted rain water. The
major purification process within the retention pond is sedimentation. During the
sedimentation suspended solids will be removed by gravitation. Settling of these sorts of
particles will remove inorganic as well as organic pollution. However, it is recommended
to provide oil skimmers at the top of these ponds for removal of oil that would be
appeared at the surface of the pond during the sedimentation process. Proposed plan
for provision of the pond will be considered during the detailed design stage.
To protect the western side of the project from expected flood from the existing nullah, a
protection dike will also be provided. The expected flood run off has been estimated and
mentioned in the revised engineering design report (section 4.5.2). In case of Hisare
Shahi the expected flood run off shall be directly disposed off from, the N-E side of the
dyke. The height of the proposed protection dyke has been kept at 1.5 to 2.0 m whereas
the depth of flow during flood will vary from 0.3 to 0.5m.
3-8



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
3.6.3   Solid Waste Management System
In case of new industrial establishments, solid waste generation rate can not be judged,
because it depends on type of industry, production capacity etc. Typical commercial and
industrial generation rates are given as below:
Office building:  0.5-1.1 kg/worker/day
Restaurant  :     0.2-0.8 kg/worker/day
Industrial        0.4-1.6 kg/worker/day
It is expected that about 5000 to 8000 workers in each phase shall be employed in
industrial park based on 50 to 75 workers/ha. The estimated generation based on 1.0
kg/worker/day will be about 5 to 8 tons/day/phase or total 10 to 16 tones/day. The solid
waste management system will involve different operations include Collection, Storage,
Transportation, Transfer Station and Disposal of Waste At this stage site for landfill has
not yet been identified by AISA. This matter shall be worked out before the process of
disbursement for timely completion of the project. Therefore, it is highly recommended
that a legal agreement between AISA and World Bank shall be developed that states the
landfill site will in any case be identified before the disbursement process. Details of solid
waste management system have been discussed in Chapter-5.
3.6.4   Fire Fighting
A pressurized fire water distribution network, comprising of pipes, fire hydrants, gate
valves, air valves, washouts etc. will be provided. The system shall be operated
automatically in case the pressure is dropped in the network by operating any fire
hydrant. Two hydrants each of 500 gpm discharge capacity can be operated at a time.
Three pumps (two duty and one standby each of 500 gpm capacity), one jockey pump of
50 gpm capacity shall be installed in the pump room. The minimum pressure
requirement at the fire hose shall be 4.5 bars. The minimum pipe size in the fire fighting
network shall be 200 mm.
3.7   Construction Material
As the Project is at master panning and preliminary design stage, so no quantities of the
construction material are available at this stage. However the main materials used for
construction of infrastructural works of the proposed Project will include coarse
aggregates, fine aggregates (sand), earth, water, asphalt, cement and steel. In general,
the contractor will identify quarry areas for coarse and fine aggregates and borrow areas
for earth material. The final approval will be given by the Engineer in the light of the
quality of the material and environmental consideration for the quarry areas and its
transportation. However, the present situation for the availability of these materials is
discussed as under:
* No borrow of large quantities of earth material are expected for the Project as
earth material extracted from trenching of water supply and sewage water
pipelines will be used for road embankment.
* Course aggregate material will probably be available locally by installing crushers
for crushing the stones. Few petty crushers have been observed near the vicinity
of the Project Area.
* As far as fine aggregate (sand) material is concerned, it will be transported from
Kabul River passing about 10 km from the Project site.
3-9



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                               AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
* Cement, steel and asphalt will be transported from Pakistan through Torkham
Border.
*Although a perennial canal flows at distance of about 1.25km from the Project
site, but no surface water will be available for construction purposes of the
Project as there is already sparse of water in the area. It is proposed that
Contractor will install a tubewell prior to start of construction activities to meet the
camp site and construction water requirements.

CHAPTER 4 - ENVIRONMENTAL AND SOCIAL BASELINE CONDITIONS
4.1   Project Area & Study Area
This Chapter describes the environmental and social baseline settings of the proposed
Project Area with respect to physical, biological and social parameters. For the purpose
of the environmental and social survey in the vicinity of the Project Area, a Study Area
was delineated based on the potential impacts due to implementation of the Project. For
this purpose in general a radius of 2 km from Project site was delineated as Study Area.
However, in case of some particular parameter, if potential impact was envisaged
beyond 2 km, information was also gathered upto that distance to foresee the impact.
Figure 4.1 provides the salient baseline features of the Project Area as well as Study
Area.
4.2   Physical Environment
Following section describes the major features of physical environment of the Project
Site.
4.2.1   Topography
The Project Area is a part of piedmont plain of the western part of Nangarhar valley
extending west to east direction. The top soil layer in and around the Project Area is
comprised of admixture of clayey silt/sandy silt with kankars, gravels, cobbles and
boulders belonging to metamorphic and igneous rocks. The color of the rocks are
ranging from white (marble) to dark black (quartzite) and are rounded to sub-rounded
indicates the fluvial (torrential) depositional environment.
The hills are part of the Hindukush range and are jaggard and precipitous, devoid of
trees and with scant grass or herb cover.
Salt range and Hindukush have been grouped into one range, on the basis that they
belong to Hindukush system of disturbances. The northern range is the Koh-i-Sufaid,
which runs eastward from the neighborhood of Kabul, forming the south side of the
valley of the Kabul River, till it ends in Pakistan territory
4.2.2   Geology
The Summer Khel mountain range lies in north and northwest of the Project Area at a
distance of about 2 to 3 kilometers and extends towards northeast direction. The
exposed rocks in north of the Project Area is of schist type (in between shale and slate
of metamorphic origin). While in northwest of the Project Area, the rock (schist) is
overtopped by the shale and then debris of sedimentary origin along the descending
slope of the mountain. The general strike of the rocks in the area is east-west and dip
towards north. Usually the rocks are bare and contain very little soil cover. The rocks are
generally of metamorphic nature, consisting of shale, phyllites and slates. Igneous
intrusions in the form of sills, mainly dolerites are met with frequently.
4.2.3  Soil
The valley area consists of Haro formations, comprising of clays, conglomerates and
gravel. The soil is mostly an alluvium or piedmont plain. These areas consist of fertile silt
washed down from the hills. Tract is suitable for agricultural crops with the help of
4-1



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
irrigation and can supports cash crops, vegetables and fruit orchards. Surrounding hills
consist of brown shale, which is being transformed into slate due to various natural
factors.
4.2.4   Seismology
The project lies in the area of seismic zone, characterized as "Major Damage Probable"
and needs every precaution while constructing buildings to minimize the seismic
impacts. Construction design and material should be in conformity with the standards
prescribed for such areas. (Seismic risk areas of Afghanistan, National Atlas of
Afghanistan, published by Geokart, Poland).
4.2.5   Climate
The climate of the area is extreme. In general, the Study Area has cold winters and hot
summers, typical of a semi-arid steppe climate. The mountainous areas far from the
proposed site are much colder than the plain areas, usually raining season begins
between July and September and bringing maritime tropical air masses with humidity
and rains.
Climate of the area varies considerably from season to season. The Study Area has hot
and dry summer and cold winter season. It has an average rainfall of about 30 to 35 cm.
Much of the rain falls during the winter season (December to February) and some in
summer season (July-September). Flow of rain fed rivers crossing the Study Area is due
to these rains and the melting of snow during the hot season.
The mean temperature of the area varies between 40C to 460C during the months of
December and June respectively. During the winter, from November to February, the
wind blows steadily from the west, often bringing dust storms.
4.2.6   Hydrology
The elevation of the Project Area ranges from 465 m to 545 m from mean sea level with
a gradient of 1.5 to 2 % in south-east to north-east direction. The area is semi flat and no
proper drainage system exists in the Project Area. However, a localize drain originates
some where in western part of the area and passes at 200 to 250 meters away from the
western corner of the Project Area and lead to north eastern direction towards the
mountainous area.
4.2.7   Water Sources
Surface and groundwater both sources are available in and around the Project Area.
The detail of each is as below;
a).   Surface Water
The surface water source is available only in the Study Area. A perennial Nangarhar
canal emerges from the under ground in north western corner of the Project Area at a
distance of about 1.5 km, passes near the northeast and eastern boundary and moves
towards south to the southern part of the valley. The discharge of the canal is reported
to 50 cumecs (1786 cusecs). Since, the source of this canal is snow covered mountains,
therefore, the canal water was cleared, free from suspended material and water quality
(electric conductivity) checked at site was 159 uS at 28.1 C 0 temperature.
The slope of the Project Area is towards east and south east direction, therefore canal
irrigates only on the left bank of the area through number of outlets. The Project Area
4-2



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
located on right bank of canal is of higher level. Therefore, any water supply from the
canal to the Project Area will need lift pumping. The canal is unlined and the reported
closure period for canal is the month of December every year.
b).   Groundwater Source
The Project Area is totally barren and the top soil layer of the Project Area and its all
surrounding comprises of admixture of clayey silt/sandy silt with kankars, gravels
cobbles and boulders of igneous and metamorphic origin. There are no springs, no open
wells, karazes are available in and around the Project Area.
During Afghan War, the area was used for refugee camp and United Nations High
Communion Refugee (UNHCR) had installed 6 water supply tube wells in 1995 for the
refugee camp through an international NGO called DACAAR, which was responsible for
the construction of water supply system for UNHCR.
Therefore no data and report for groundwater is available for the Project Area except the
presence of these tube wells.
During the field visit, all the existing operative and abandoned water points located in
and around the Project Area were visited for their data. The detail of the inventory is
given in the Table-4.1 and location of tubewells has been shown in Figure-4.1.
Table-4.1 indicates that 4 No. tubewells out of the total 6 have been filled up with stones
by locals. The remaining tube wells , one is being operated by a private contractor for
the water supply and sell water to refugees which still live in the Kabul camp, while the
other tubewell located closed to the Project Area is being used by a factory owner.
The technical data, such as strata chart, water table design of the tube wells and specific
capacity data along with capacity and pump setting of these tubewells could not be
traced from any agencies including UNHCR and IRC etc.
However, a representative of IRC office Jalalabad which has been a part of team during
construction and later on in-charge of water supply system of Kabul camp, reported that
depth of all six tubewells was 110 m (361 ft) each and 27 m (90 ft) PVC strainer was
provided at bottom. Whereas, 80 m (260 ft) MS housing pipes of diameter 10 inches was
provided at top in each of the tubewells. He also reported that the maximum water table
in the area was 45 meters (148 ft).
As far as the potential of the tubewells is concerned, he reported that pumps installed in
each tubewells had been yielding 112,000 litres in 4 hours or 7.7 litres/s to each sector
of the camps.
As per his statement, the tube wells had worked satisfactory for about three years for the
water supply of about 40,000 refugees and there had been no problem with discharge of
any tubewell.
During the inventory, water table in the operative tubewell No-1, located near southern
boundary of the Project Area was checked and found at 34 meter (112 ft) ntural surface
level (nsl). The next operative tunewell-3 located about 2 km west of the Project Area
had no opening for measurement of water table due to fixing of a plate over tubewell.

4.2.8   Water Quality
i).   Existing Water Pollution Sources
Proposed industrial site is a piece of land of abandoned houses of immigrants from
Pakistan. Since it is an abandoned site no anthropogenic activities exist there.
Generally, Project Area is free from any pollution sources. However, area around the site
(Study Area) contributes in pollution, which directly or indirectly effects the Project Area.
Since there is no proper sewerage system exists in the area, so domestic sewage which
is allowed to discharge into the open land. Land is dry and waste water evaporates due
to hot weather conditions. The quantity of domestic sewage produced is very small as
the water is a not easily available in the Study Area.
Majority of the people of the area used open field toilets and storm water produced by
rains flashes the garbage into the surface water resources, which contaminate the water
quality.
There is no proper solid waste management system in the area. Solid waste produced is
of domestic nature and mostly composed of garbage (putricible waste), polyethylene
bags, plastic bottles, beverage cans, plastic and paper etc. Locals are not aware of solid
waste management hence one can see these items laying in the form of humps at
different places in the Study Area near residential areas. No hazardous waste was
observed at site as Study Area is free from any industrial activity.
ii).  Receiving Water Quality
In order to investigate the quality of receiving water sources, water samples were
collected from Nangarhar Canal, tube wells and hand pumps (Figure-4.1 shows the
water sample locations of the Study Area).
The water samples were preserved as per US, EPA methods and transported to
Pakistan for physical and chemical analysis against various important parameters for
drinking water quality. Since Afghanistan has no drinking water quality standards these
results of water samples were compared WHO drinking water quality guidelines. Results
and comparison of water samples is presented in Appendix-A from Table A-1 to A-4.
Surface Water Quality
There is only one source of surface water in the Study Area which is the Nangarhar
Canal. Due to non-availability of any tubewell or hand pump, residents of Choragali
village are using canal water as drinking water. Sampling of canal water was carried out
at three locations and tested against 22 basic parameters for drinking water quality.
Analysis shows that canal water is not fit for drinking purpose due to higher values of
turbidity, total coliform, e-coli and color. Presence of total colifrom and e-coli shows that
the water is highly contaminated and prone to various water borne diseases.
Ground Water Quality
There are no operational tube wells or hand pumps in the Project Area. Hence ground
water sample from pump located adjacent to Project Area in the Plastic Factory was
collected. It was tested and compared with WHO drinking water quality standards.
Analysis shows that water is fit for drinking purpose as all the major parameters of
drinking water quality are within the WHO guideline values and no presence of total
coliform, e-coli was observed.
4-5



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
4.2.9  Ambient Air Quality
i). Existing Sources of Ambient Air Pollution
Project site is located about 200 meters from the Torkham-Jalalabad road. Sources of
air pollution for Carbon mono-oxide (CO), Nitrogen dioxides (NO2), smoke and
Hydrocarbons (HC) is the transport plying over the Torkham-Jalalabad road. The
pollution load of these air contaminants is higher in day time as mostly traffic exists in
the day time. Source of Particulate Matter (PM) pollution is the blowing wind. Dust is the
major pollution at site since there is not much vegetation and grass cover on the site and
adjoining areas due to the non-availability of water.
ii). Quality of Ambient Air
In order to establish the ambient air quality base line conditions, monitoring was carried
out within Project Area as well as Study Area at 18 locations (Figure-4.1 shows the
location of Air Quality Monitoring points). The ambient air quality parameters, which were
covered during monitoring, include CO, NO2, SO2 and Particulate Matter (PM).
Ambient Air Quality for SO2, NO2 and CO was monitored at seven locations in the
Project Area. Results show that maximum values of SO2, NO2 and CO were 45.7, 36.9
and 690 ppb respectively.
Similarly, Ambient Air Quality was monitored around the Project Area within the Study
Area. Measurements were made along the Nangarhar canal and along the Torkham-
Jalalabad road. The maximum values of SO2, NO2 and CO along the Torkham-Jalalabad
road were 105.8, 80 and 1240 ppb respectively. The increase in values is due to the
presence of traffic on the road. Similarly maximum values of SO2, NO2 and CO along the
Nangarhar canal were 45.7, 43 and 710 ppb respectively which show lack of traffic and
other pollution sources. Results of ambient air quality monitored are presented in
Appendix-A, Table A -5 to A-7.
As compared to the International Air Quality Standards (see Table A-8 at Appendix-A)
the existing ambient air quality is more or less within permissible limits).
PM monitoring was carried out at 13 points in the Project Area and Study Area along the
Nangarhar Canal and Torkham-Jalalabad Road. The maximum values of PM
concentrations were 310 and 1780 ppb respectively. In general the PM concentrations
are on higher side due to lack of vegetation or grass cover on ground along with
abandoned mud houses within as well as outside the Project Area. However, it is
expected that PM will be within the permissible limit as prescribed in International
Standards (see Table A-9 to A-11, at Appendix A).
4.2.10 Noise Levels
i). Existing Sources of Noise Pollution
There are two main sources of pollution in the vicinity of the Project Area i.e. vehicles on
Torkham-Jalalabad road and Cement-Asphalt Plant. No other sources of noise
generation were observed in the Project Area as well as Study Area.
ii).  Noise Level Monitoring
To establish the noise level baseline conditions in the area, monitoring was carried out at
different locations within the Project Area as well as Study Area  (Figure-4.1  shows
the noise level monitoring points and Table A-12, Appendix-A provides the results of
4-6



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
monitoring points.). The maximum Leq calculated for Project Area during morning and
afternoon is 68.16 and 79.88 dB(A) respectively. This point is located near the Torkham-
Jalalabad Road and higher value is due to the high volume of traffic on the road.
Leq calculated for five locations along the Torkham-Jalalabad Road and for six locations
along the Nangarhar Canal with the Study Area. The maximum Leq value was recorded
79 dB (A). The high values of noise back ground levels were due to the high volume of
traffic on the road. As compared to Pakistan NEQS noise limit of 85 dB(A), the existing
noise levels in the area are within permissible limits.
Photographic record of the physical features of the site is attached in the Photologs
(Photo 1 to 7 and 11).
4.3   Ecological Environment
4.3.1   Flora
i).   General
The area falls in arid zone, characterized by low rainfall, scarcity of moisture, and long
dry spells hence natural vegetation consists of mostly xerophytes species. There are low
forests of thorny and branchy trees, scattered singly or in small groups with a large
number of shrubs and bushes. Hills being shale or slate formations lack soil cover and
are without any vegetation except small shrubs and herbs found mostly in depressions
where some soil has accumulated.
ii).  Trees
There are no tall trees in the Project Area. Trees exist in the vicinity of the project area or
Study Area especially along Nangarhar Canal, its branches and along the boundaries of
agricultural fields and fruit orchards, where excessive planting has been carried out.
Mostly Eucalyptus, Shisham, Mulberry and Bottle brush have been planted. Table-4-2
shows the kind of trees raised in the vicinity of the Project Area.

iii).  Shrubs, Herbs and Grasses
The Project Area has nearly 40% cover of grasses. Grass is extensively over-grazed
and is now in a retarded and degraded form.
The main species are chemer (Elusine compressa), Khabal (Cynodon dactylon) and
Kana (Saccharum munja). Kana is found in low lying areas and depressions, where the
moisture is retained for a longer period of time. Typha grass (Typha angustata) is found
mostly along water channels and in marshy areas, outside the project area. Shrubs
found in the area include Calatropis (Calatropis procera), which is a poisonous plant and
is present in large numbers. It is strong indicator of overgrazing due to which palatable
species have vanished. Shrubs/herbs commonly found in the area are Jaroo or Gaz
(Equisetum arvensis), Sperke (Mentha arvensis) Khar (Haloxylon recurvum), Camel
Thorn (Alhagi maurorum) etc. All these herbs/shrubs are mostly found in depressions,
formed by the inhabitants using the camp, during their stay. A list of shrubs, herbs and
grasses found in the Project Area and its vicinity are given in the Table 4.3 and 4.4.

iv).  National Parks, Reserves and Protected Areas
There are no national parks, reserves or protected areas in the vicinity of the Project
Area even upto 10 km from the Project Site.
v).   Rare or Endangered Species of Flora
No rare and endangered species was observed and neither reported by the locals as
well as officials of the agriculture department at Jalalabad.
vi).   Agriculture
No agriculture is being practiced in the Project Area due to non-availability of water.
Agriculture is practiced in the northern and eastern side of the Project Area, where the
land is irrigated by Nangarhar Canal and its branches, which is the source of water
supply for agriculture and livestock.
Wheat is the staple crop and national food. In the north of the Project Area, a large
number of agricultural fields exist, where only wheat is raised during November-
December, and harvested during May. The fields remain fallow during rest of the year.
Jawar, cotton and vegetables are raised in the adjoining areas in the southern and
eastern parts. Fodder crops such as berseem and Lucerne are grown abundantly in
these areas to cater for the needs of their livestock.
vii).  Fodder
Leguminous fodders are traditional crops throughout in the Study Area, wherever
irrigation water is available. Fodder is usually grown close to the homestead and is partly
fed fresh and partly made into hay to supplement the crop residues, which forms the
basis of winter (and dry season) feed. Lucerne (Medicago sativa) is the most wide
spread, where perennial irrigation water is available. Shaftal (Trifolium resupinatum) is
grown as winter annual and gives two hay cuts in spring. Berseem (T. alexandrium) is
also grown in the vicinity of the Project Area and is popular in the area due to its higher
production.

Flissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
viii). Horticulture
There are a number of orchards on canal side in the vicinity of the Project Area. Olive
orchards exist towards the south and eastern side of the Project Area, while Plum, Citrus
and Guava orchards exist on the western side. As per information, supplied by the canal
department, olive orchards are present over an area of 22,000 ha in the vicinity of the
Project Area, whereas citrus fruit has been raised on nearly 75 ha. Guava and Plum
have been raised on experimental basis on small areas and are doing well.

Natural fauna of the area comprises mammals, reptiles, insects and birds etc.
