of Afghanistan, including any amendments from time to time.
7.12.8  Role of Other Functionaries
A.    Role of National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA)
The National Environmental Protection Agency (NEPA) is a regulatory authority and
mainly responsible to develop and implement national environmental policies and
strategies in order to integrate environmental issues and sustainable development
approaches into the legal and regulatory frameworks. NEPA is also responsible to
assess the effectiveness of the implementation of the environmental legislations and
regulations to improve the sustainability of the use and management of natural
resources and the effectiveness of measures for conservation and rehabilitation of the
environment. Similarly, Afghanistan Environmental Protection Act, empowers the NEPA
to take legal action against the non-compliance of environmental legislations and
regulations and penalties may be imposed from cancellation of license to six months
imprisonment, or payment of a cash fine equivalent to the damage caused or even both.
As NEPA is a regulatory authority and its main function is to develop and implement the
national environmental policies, so its working in the proposed IP Project will be as an
independent monitoring agency. NEPA will inspect the Project at its own convenience or
on receipt of compliant from any person or NGO about non-compliance of any
environmental legislation or its part.
7-45



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
B.    District Administration
The proposed industrial park site is located under the jurisdiction of Rodat District which
is out of Jalalabad Municipality limits. Although Afghan Environmental Act empowers the
District Administration to monitor the Project activities to ensure the implementation of
local regulations for land use, conservation of natural vegetation, air, water and land
pollution, the disposal of solid waste and waste of effluents as well as matters related to
public health and safety. But unfortunately District Councils have not established any
regulations as yet in this regard. However, in future as the regulations will be on board,
District Council will monitor the Project activities to ensure the compliance of those
regulations and AISA will adhere to those legislations and regulations.
Currently, no technical staff is available in Rodat District to handle the developmental
works in the area. In addition to the formulation of legislations and regulations for
management of land use, conservation of natural resources and infrastructure
developmental works at district level, it is also highly desirable to establish planning and
designing sections supported by adequate technical staff and logistic arrangements. A
comprehensive institutional capacity building plan is recommended for the district
administration.
7.12.9  Proposed Training Program
A.    Technical Assistance
An environmental training and technical assistance (TA) program should be carried out
to enhance the capability of IPDA, NEPA and District Administration to effectively
implement this EMMP, as well as to facilitate the improved environmental management
of future industrial parks projects by increasing the environmental awareness of staff in
general. Initially, the training program will target a small portion of the IPDA and EPA
staff directly associated with the project, but this is expected to trigger a process that will
enable the IPDA and NEPA to integrate environmental issues into its day-to-day
operations and project management, and into future developmental projects.
NEPA is a newly established agency and having Provincial Offices as well, but there is
no availability of environmental monitoring equipment, staff and other office equipment.
During a detailed meeting at NEPA's Provincial Office of Jalalabad, it was observed that
no technical staff, office equipment, computers, laboratory, and other environmental
monitoring equipment, etc. was available. Awareness about the roles and functions of
the NEPA was also lacking to the Provincial Office Staff. The situation demands to
strengthen the capacity and capability of regional office through logistic support,
providing concerned technical staff and with in house and abroad trainings to key staff
regarding environmental management, monitoring and auditing.
The AISA will engage a short-term Expatriate Environmental Specialist (ES) to manage
the environmental training program. The objective of the TA will be to help establish
appropriate systems i.e. HSE, EMS, and to train ESPO, EO and other senior IPDA and
staff of other line departments responsible for managing environment, operations, and
planning, who can then impart training at a broader level within and outside their
departments (i.e., the training of trainers). The ES will organize foreign and in-country
training courses for IPDA and NEPA staff; train them in specialized areas such as land,
water, air and noise pollutions; develop environment operation manuals, and train other
IPDA staff in applying these manuals. The training protocols will be prepared by the ES
for both environmental and social training. The main indicators will include the following:
.                                 7-46



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
Environmental Protocols
. Procedures for monitoring air quality parameters and measures to be adopted for
avoiding or minimizing air pollution, particularly from asphalt plant, haul tracks,
haul-trucks, blasting, etc.
. Procedures for monitoring water quality parameters and measures to be adopted
for avoiding or minimizing water pollution, particularly from wastewater effluent
from workshop, machinery washing yard, and campsite, and from dumping of
spoil material from excavation and landslide load and asphalt and other
obnoxious chemicals.
* Noise levels from construction machinery, blasting, etc.
* Protection and conservation of biological resources and enhancement of
environment by providing compensatory plantation.
Social Protocols
* Safety hazards for workforce and local communities arising from construction
activities, blasting, road crossing, etc.
. Use of safety gadgets by the workforce.
* Interruption of access of local people to natural resources and to places of
socioeconomic activities.
* Integrity of privacy of local people particularly woman folk.
. Sanctity of religious and cultural properties.
In addition to the training arranged and imparted by the ES, the supervision consultant
will train the staff working under the project's contractors and the IPDA's regional staff, in
environmental compliance and the daily monitoring of construction projects. The cost of
this training will be included in the budget of services provided by the Supervision
Consultant.
B.    Establishment of Training Centers
Keeping in view the high demand of technical, skilled and semi skilled staff after
establishment of the industrial parks, establishment of training centers is highly
recommended. Availability of trained staff will not only attract the private investors to
establish industrial units and but also perform a significant role in human development
and poverty alleviation. In Jalalabad there are few NGOs like International Rescue
Committee (IRC), GTZ, etc. which are already providing trainings in different areas. By
providing financial assistance to enhance capacity of such NGOs, training centers can
be established easily.
7.13  Environmental Monitoring Program
7.13.1  Objectives
The objective of environmental monitoring during the Construction and Operation stages
will be as follows:
. Monitor the actual project impact on physical, biological and socioeconomic
indicators. This will indicate the adequacy of the EIA/EMMP.
* Recommend mitigation measures for any unforeseen impact or where the impact
level exceeds than that anticipated in the EIA.
. Ensure compliance with legal and community obligations including safety at
construction and operation stages.
7-47



I lissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                          AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
. Monitor the rehabilitation of borrow areas and the restoration of the construction
campsite as described in the EMMP.
. Ensure the safe disposal of excess construction materials, solid waste, effluents
and gaseous emissions.
The main objectives of monitoring during the operation phase will be to:
.Appraise the adequacy of the EIA with respect to the project's predicted long-
term impacts on the area's physical, biological and socioeconomic environment.
. Evaluate the effectiveness of the mitigation measures proposed in the EMMP,
and recommend improvements in the EMMP, if required.
* Compile periodic incidents/accident data to support analyses that will help
minimize future risks.
* Monitor the survival rate of proposed plantations.
AISA will ensure two types of monitoring during the execution of the Project activities. (i)
Compliance Monitoring - to ensure that proposed measures in the EMMP are adhered
to, and (ii) Effects Monitoring - to establish baseline values for environmental parameters
such as air quality, water quality and noise levels.
7.13.2  Monitoring Strategy
The monitoring of environmental activities will be carried out by the Supervisory
Consultants (SC) and compliance and effects monitoring will be carried out by AISA as
Internal Monitoring agency. The ESPO and EO working under the AISA/IPDA head
office and regional office respectively, will supervise all the SC activities in the field.
ESPO and EO will also ensure the public participation. The agencies involved for
monitoring and their roles and responsibilities will be as under:
A. Implementation and Monitoring
i).   Construction Contractor
Physical implementation of the EMMP is the sole responsibility of the Contractor during
construction stage. Contractor will be responsible for in-house monitoring to ensure that
the construction activities are being carried out as specified in EMMP.
ii)   Supervisory Consultant
The Supervisory Consultant will be responsible for environmental monitoring and will
perform the following activities.
 Monitoring of the environmental aspects of projects during construction to ensure
that the environmental requirements of the contract and the mitigation measures
proposed in the EMMP are implemented.
. Undertake critically important routine visual monitoring of construction, waste
disposal and overall environmental management practices by the Contractor(s).
Effective environmental management during construction will require frequent
site visits and observation skills.
*A systematically check of noise levels using a portable noise meter operated
near major construction equipment and machinery as specified in Table 7.2.
. Visual checks of exhaust emissions from equipment and vehicles on a daily basis
.Visual checks of airborne dust on temporary access roads, material stockpiles,
disturbed soil, and haul tracks.
7-48



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
* Instrumental monitoring of water, ambient air and noise levels as per intensity
and frequency specified in Table 7.2.
* To maintain the monitoring records and submit monthly reports to AISA
describing the details of environmental monitoring parameters, non-compliance
of the Contractor and actions taken for rectification.
B.    Auditing
The audit of the proposed Project will be carried out both by internally by AISA and
externally by NEPA. The primary aim of the auditing is to assess compliance and
effectiveness of the EMMP as well as the alternative environmental and social
objectives, and also to assess the effectiveness of previous corrective actions. Audit will
also suggest remedial measures to overcome the environmental and social problems.
Following are the main objectives of the audit.
*To evaluate whether the monitoring done by Supervisory Consultants is in
compliance with the targets as set in EIA/EMMP.
. To determine the conformity of the environmental and social management plans
with specified requirements and identify non-conformity in environmental and
social parameters as per EIA/EMMP.
* Meet regulatory requirements and commitments.
i).   Internal Auditing by AISA/IPDA
AISA/IPDA will be responsible for internal auditing and will ensure the compliance of
environmental monitoring protocols by the Contractor as well as Supervisory
Consultants. ESPO and EO staff to be appointed by the AISA/IPDA will be responsible
for internal monitoring. As AISA has no experience of environmental monitoring and
neither they have the equipment. It is recommended that Project should provide the
handy equipment to monitor the environmental parameters at site like noise meter, DO
meter, EC meter, pH meter, etc. A provision has already been made under the Project
for such equipment. AISA will also be responsible for coordination with NEPA, NGOs
and other Government Agencies.
ii).  External Auditing by NEPA
Being a regulatory authority, NEPA will audit the Project activities as an independent
monitoring/auditing agency to ensure the adherence of the national legislation and
regulations related with environment. NEPA will inspect the Project at its own
convenience or on receipt of complaint from any person or NGO about non-compliance
of any environmental legislation or its part. AISA will facilitate the NEPA for monitoring.
As NEPA is a newly born organization and they do not have the laboratory equipment,
technicians, etc. It is recommended that Project should finance laboratory for the NEPA
and other necessary equipment. Annexure-VI provides the staff required and cost of
laboratory equipment required by the NEPA.
7.13.3  Monitoring Parameters and Frequency
The major negative impacts of the Project activities are related to water resources,
ambient air and noise levels generation. Impacts on biological environment are
insignificant. However, impacts related the socio-economic and cultural environment are
related to employment opportunities to the locals, usage of common resources by
7-49



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
contractor, and other cultural conflicts related with outsider workers. The details of
monitoring parameters are as under:
i).   Physical Environment
For physical environment following parameters will be monitored:
* Ambient air quality (mainly NO2, SO2, CO and PM10)
* Asphalt plant emissions (smoke, dust, etc.)
* Ambient noise levels
* Water quality (drinking and surface water)
Table 7.2 provides the parameters to be monitored, standards to be followed, intensity
and frequency of monitoring.
ii).  Biological Environment
As referred earlier that there are no significant impacts on biological environment, so no
monitoring during construction activities will be required except to check that Contractor
should not cut the existing trees in study area to meet fire or any other requirements at
campsite. During operation stage, monitoring will be required to observe the generation
and growth of new plantation to be carried out by the Project.
iii).  Socio-economic Environment
Effects on the socio-economic environment will be monitored by ESPO considering
parameters like hiring of local employment, health and safety of communities, mobility of
local women etc. The Supervisory Consultant at construction stage and ESPO at
operation stage will maintain a Social Complaints Register. Chapter-8 of this report
covers the socio-economic environment and recommends a detailed social assessment
study to be conducted. It is proposed that recommendations proposed by that social
assessment report should be incorporated in this EMMP for the monitoring of social
parameters.
iv).  Post-Project Monitoring
After completion of the development phase post-project monitoring will be carried out.
The objective of this monitoring will be to determine the level of residual impacts of the
project on physical, biological and socio-economic environment of the Project Area. The
monitoring may be carried out within one month after the end of all activities in the
Project Area. The post-project survey report will be submitted within one month after
completion of the survey. As part of the post-project monitoring field monitors will also
check restoration of sites restored at that time according to the requirements of the EIA.
Supervisory Consultant in consultation with AISA and NEPA staff will conduct the visit
and will submit the report to AISA.
7.14  Communication and Documentation Plan
7.14.1  Kick-Off Meeting
One kick off meeting will take place among AISA, SC and Contractor before the start of
construction. The purpose of this kick off meeting will be to demonstrate the regulatory
and monitoring requirements prior to the start of the individual project activities have
been met.
7-50



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
7.14.2  Meetings and Reports
Monthly meetings will be held during the construction phase at the construction camp.
The purpose of these meetings will be to discuss the activities of the last month, non-
compliances noted by SC and AISA and their remedial measures. The meeting will be
chaired by the representative nominated by AISA. The meeting will be recorded in the
form of a Monthly Environmental Report (MER) to be prepared by SC and reviewed by
AISA. The report will include but not limited to:
* Summary of project activities during last month;
* SC monitors and AISA and contractors environmental representatives present
onsite;
* Summary of monitoring activities;
* Non-compliances observed and mitigation measures taken or required.
The MER will be communicated to the AISA, NEPA and Contractor's Representative.

7.14.3 Social Complaints Register
The SC will maintain a register of complaints received from local communities and
measures taken to mitigate these concerns. All community complaints received will be
sent to the ESPO of the AISA for further action.
7.14.4  Change Record Register
All changes to the EMMP or the project will be handled through the Change
Management Plan referred earlier. During construction stage, SC will be responsible to
maintain the change record register while during operation stage, EO working at regional
office will maintain the register along with date, type of change, persons responsible for
change and action taken to get approval for change from competent authority.
7.14.5  Final Monitoring Report
A final monitoring report will be prepared by SC in collaboration with AISA after the post
project monitoring. The report should address the following:
. Introduction;
* Scope, Methodology, and Monitoring Team;
a Details of the Project Activities;
* Natural Resource Use by the Project;
. Record and Statistical Analysis of Non-compliances;
* Effects of the Project on Wildlife, Communities and Physical Resources;
* Recommendations for Future Projects.
7.14.6  Photographic Record
SC and the contractor will maintain a photographic record of all areas to be used during
the implementation of the project. As a minimum the photographic record will include the
photographs of the sites, access track, camp sites, and monitoring of different
categories.
7.15  Document Control
The purpose of document control is to ensure that documents are controlled so that only
the latest authorized version of the documents is used. All documents shall be dated and
assigned a Document Control Number indicating the version. This is to ensure the most
up-to-date version is in use. Each EMMP Procedure and records shall be signed by the
AISA as the 'issuer'. The original version of each document shall be kept in the official
file drawer at AISA regional office and one copy at head office. When these will be
finalized from all concerned, these shall be are to be filed with the AISA regional office.
Electronic files shall be saved on the shared directory. The current version is to be saved
in a folder labeled "Current" and the older versions are saved in a folder labeled
"Archived" and marked as 'Obsolete', for future reference.
7.16  Environmental Management and Monitoring Cost
7.16.1  Environmental Management Cost
Environmental management cost related with the mitigation measures of environmental
parameters related to the location of camp site facilities, construction activities, borrow
I7-57



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                              AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
material, etc. will be the sole responsibility of the Contractor and he will take care of cost
implications as it will be the part of his contract agreement.
The Project's environmental management cost related with the construction of
environmental mitigation infrastructure like waste water treatment plant, solid waste
management, storm  water drainage, provisions for firefighting, etc. have been
considered in Preliminary Design of the Project and will be the part of Project estimate.
In case of ambient air and noise generated by individual industries during operation
stage of the Project, individual industries will be responsible to provide the
treatment/mitigations at source to follow the standards prescribed in EMMP. So cost will
be borne by individual investors.
Operation and Maintenance cost of the environmental mitigation infrastructure will be
borne by the AISA at initial stage and when industrial park will be fully established, will
be charged from individual industries as per their contribution of the effluents.
Methodology will be evaluated by the AISA at operation stage in consultation with private
investors. 0 & M cost for initial stage of environmental mitigation infrastructure has been
included in Project Estimate.
7.16.2  Environmental Monitoring Cost
The environmental monitoring at pre-construction stage and other in-house monitoring to
be carried out by the Contractor will be the part of his contract agreement.
Similarly, the environmental monitoring to be carried out during construction stage by the
SC will be the part of their contract agreement.
Cost for Internal Monitoring/Auditing to be carried out by the AISA staff including
purchase of required equipment has been included in the Project budget.
7.16.3  Training Cost
The Project training cost has been included in the Project budget to hire the services of
Expatriate Environmental Specialist, ESPO, EO, to provide training to AISA, NEPA and
Local Administration Staff.

EIA Report
CHAPTER 8 - SOCIAL ASSESSMENT
8.1   Socio-Economic Environment
Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park is located near Jalalabad City in Rodat District, Province
Nangarhar. The villages around Hissar-e-Shahi Site (Project area) are listed below;
a  Hissar-e-Shahi Camp
I  Kabul Camp
* Chora Gali
*  Nachaabad
The brief overview of the above villages found in the project and study area has been
explained one by one.
Hissar-e-Shahi Camp
Hissar-e-Shahi camp is partly located in the Project Area and partly in the Study Area.
The people living in Hissar-e-Shahi Camp are Afghan Muhajreen (Refugees) and
originally belong to Kunar Province (Afghanistan). The people have been residing at this
site for the last one and a half year and are Pashto speaking. The main occupation of
the people is labour. The camp is accessible through a dirt track and camp is located at
an approximate distance of half a kilometer (km) from the main road. Presently, about 20
families reside in the area of Hissar-e-Shahi camp that lies within the Project Area. The
camp lacks in infrastructural facilities altogether. The residents fetch water from an
existing tubewell located about 1 km from the site by paying Afghanis 50 (equivalent to
US $ 1.00) /month to the contractor. The residents are prone to water borne diseases
due to lack of sanitation facilities.
During the group discussion held in the camp area, it was learnt that the people are
happy about the proposed project but requires compensation for relocation.
Kabul Camp
Kabul Camp is located in the Study Area of Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park. It was
constructed in early nineties. The camp comprises nine blocks, and each block has 170
houses having an approximate population of 1050. The main occupants of the Kabul
camp are refugees from Pakistan who originally belonged to Pashtoon and Tajik tribes.
Pashto and Persian are the main languages spoken in the Kabul Camp. The camp is
accessible through a dirt track. There is only one Primary School for both boys and girls
near Kabul Camp. The camp lacks in institutional and civic facilities. Water for domestic
use is personally collected from a community tubewell by paying Afghanis.50 /month to
the contractor. The influentials have their own water pipes in their houses and pay
Afghanis. 350/month as water charges to the contractor. Pressing needs of Kabul
Camp are Basic Health Unit (BHU), high school, transport, electricity and potable water
etc.
Chora Gali
The village Chora Gali is located on right bank of Nangarhar Canal about 25 km from
Jalalabad city and 3 km from Highway Torkham-Jalalabad Road. Tribes residing in
Chora Gali are Afghan Muhajreen (Refugees) belonging to Mola Khail, Mian Khail and
3                                  ~8-1_                                _



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
Mulla Khail Clans. Pashto is the only language spoken in this village. Around 650
houses exist in the village having a population of 5100. Like other cases, the village
lacks in educational, institutional and civic facilities. A few residents usually shift to Kabul
City during the summer season. The Nangarhar Canal is the main source of water and
this water is used for domestic as well as drinking purposes. Main diseases in the village
are Malaria, Typhoid, Diarrohea and Tuberculosis. Maliks are the influentials of this
village. Pure drinking water, hospital, school, transport and electricity are the pressing
needs of this village.
Nachaabad
Nachaabad village is located northwest of Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park at an
approximate distance of 4.5 km. The Pashto speaking people living in this village are
basically from Rodat District and are locals. The village is accessible from proposed
Industrial Park through a dirt track whereas an independent road connects this village to
main Torkham-Jalalabad road. The main source of income is through agricultural
activities.
The only and the nearest source of surface water is Nangarhar Canal, agricultural
activities are dependent on this source. For drinking water, mostly community shallow
pumps are being utilized. The village lacks in basic amenities, infrastructure etc.
however, the living conditions of residents of this village are much better in comparison
to other villages due to agricultural activities.
Economic development crucially depends on environment and natural resources to
provide goods and services, which directly and indirectly generate socio-economic
benefits. At the same time, economic development is often accompanied by significant
adverse impacts both on the environment and the natural resources. It is clear that
successful economic development depends on the rational and sustainable use of
environmental resources and on minimization of adverse environmental impacts, as
much as feasible through proper selection, planning, designing and implementation of
mitigation measures.
Socio-economic and environmental aspects have been studied with a view to appraise
the present characteristics and to assess the impact of the proposed project. In order to
make first hand appraisal, necessary information was gathered by the consultants
through field surveys and collection of  available data from relevant departments in
Jalalabad. The study focuses mainly on demography, occupation, education, housing,
health, family income and expenditure, basic amenities, livestock, role of women,
cultural values and amount borrowed.
8.2   Data Source and Methodology
Development is not just an economic phenomenon, but is a multidimensional process
involving the recognition and re-orientation of the entire economic and social system. In
order to have an in-depth feeling of its inhabitants, it was considered appropriate to
conduct interviews with notables, stakeholders such as AISA, Project Affectees including
direct and indirect, National Environmental Directorate, Jalalabad, Ministry of Water and
Power along with district administration of Rodat District. The views of the stake-holders
were ascertained through departmental meetings, focus census, group discussions,
village profiles and public consultations/scoping sessions and hold group discussions
with cross section of the people from different settlements in Project and Study Area.
8-2



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
Efforts were made to visit people residing in above mentioned areas of the proposed
Industrial Park Project. For ascertaining the perceptions of different stakeholders about
the project (during and after the construction stage) a socio-economic sample survey
was carried out. All the stakeholders residing in the project area were interviewed in the
field, through structured questionnaires with the help of local interpreters having good
command on Pashto language. The social survey was conducted by selecting local
influentials i.e. Maliks, stakeholders from various walks of life and through group
discussions. The published data was not available in Jalalabad, hence the base line
conditions in the Project and Study Area related to the various socio-economic aspects
which were collected separately as detailed below:
8.3   Social Surveys
8.3.1   Household Survey
Twenty one households in Project Area and two hundred fifty six households were
covered in Study Area were interviewed during the field visits as shown in Table 8-1.

8.4   Analysis of Focused Census
The Project Area is located in Rodat District about 35 km from the city of Jalalabad. The
total population of Rodat District was 75,207, as per 1990 census report by the UNHCR.

members. Based on sample survey of the Project Area female and male population
worked out as 60 males and 56 females in different age groups. Female population

are 6.7 percent. Overall occupational distribution of the people showed that most of the
respondents are Laborers.

8.4.6   Sources of Drinking Water
Easy access to potable/safe drinking water is one of the basic needs. Sources of water
supply area wise are given below:
Project Area
As per information gathered in the sample survey 95.2 percent of the houses are using
water from Community Tube wells on payment and only 4.8 percent carry water from
Nangarhar Canal in Project Area.
Study Area
In the Study Area the major source of drinking water (50.4%) is also from Community
Tube wells and (49.6%) from Nangarhar Canal. Number and percentage are given in

Energy is the most important input for economic development and national prosperity.
During the field visit it is observed that not a single house has the facility of electricity in
the Project and Study Area.
8.4.7   Electricity
Energy is the most important input for economic development and national prosperity.
During the field visit it is observed that 100 percent of houses have no facility of
electricity in Project and Study Area.
8.4.8   Sanitation/Drainage Facilities
No proper sanitation/drainage facilities are available in the Project and Study Area.
Waste water is disposed of in the open spaces just outside the houses to dry off.

EIA Report
Telephone, Post Office, or metalled road facilities are not available in the Project and
Study Area. However, these facilities are available in Jalalabad city.
8.5   Other Facilities
8.5.1   Education
In the Social Sector, educational facilities are the most important requirement. Given the
level of development in the area, most of the areas are without such facilities. There is
only one school in the Study Area located in the Kabul Camp which is used both by girls
and boys. Prejudice against female education is strong and most of the respondents
considered that educating girls make them unfit for their true function in life. School
building is in dilapidated condition.
8.5.2   Public Health
Health facilities are quite inadequate. There are only two private dispensaries and two
private clinics in the Study Area. The people in the Project and Study Area have a
tendency to get treatment from traditional Faith Healers, due to lack of suitable and
sufficient health facilities. Bad sanitary conditions, insufficient medical facilities and
meager parental care, all contribute to the prevalence of ill health and high rate of
mortality in the Area under study. Female respondents in the area informed that there is
no lady doctor in the area and they are facing problems to go for male doctor due to the
restriction of Pardah (veil) System. People of the area have to get treatment from
Jalalabad City.
8.5.3   Role of Women
The women have no formal role in the authority structure of the villages in the Project
and Study Areas. There are no maternity homes or trained lady health visitors (LHVs) in
the villages. Three maternal death cases have been reported during the last one year.
Most of the women stay at home. They travel outside the village only in a serious
condition to get treatment from the hospital in Jalalabad City or to attend weddings of
relatives. Women in Project and the Study Area are responsible for food preparation and
to look after the children and remain fully occupied for 14-16 hours a day. Pardah (veil)
is observed by most families. The role of women will gain more importance due to the
increased activity in all the socio-economic and socio-cultural fields in the Study Area.
8.5.3.1 Women Concerns and Perceptions about the Project
During the socio-economic survey Consultant team faced various problems in
conducting female consultations. Based on Consultant's previous experience in
Afghanistan such as "Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA) of Torkham-Jalalabad
Road", "Environmental and Social Impact Assessment (E&SIA) of Jalalabad Bypass",
"Resettlement Action Plan (RAP) of Jalalabad Bypass" and "Environmental and Social
Assessment (E & SIA) of Kabul-Sarobi Road". It is extremely difficult to conduct
consultation with women in Afghanistan due to their rigid religious and cultural beliefs.
Same situation was faced by the Consultants. However with great difficulty, the
consultants managed to conduct consultation with 11 women. The findings of those
consultations are described in subsequent paragraphs:
Routine life of a woman revolves around her home and children. The activities in which
they are involved in are; fetching water, cooking food, collection of fire wood, washing
clothes and utensils. Social status of women is not better. They do not have equal rights
8-9



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
in legacy and effectives say in the routine life matters. Women of the area are in quite
miserable condition due to the non-availability of basic amenities, especially in health
sector.
Although the women consulted were all illiterate, yet they expressed their main problems
and the perceptions about the project very clearly. The most pressing needs of the
women of Hissar-e-Shahi and their perceptions about the project are summed up  as
under: Provision of basic health facilities ranked as the most pressing need of women of
the area.
The second most perceived pressing need was education for the girls of the area
as there is no educational facility available in the area for girls except only one
Primary School which is used for both boys and girls.
* Availability of employment opportunities was the third pressing need of women.
In addition, women have to face the difficulties to fetch water from a distance far
away from their homes; consequently, provision of sustained water supply was
considered a major hindrance for their social welfare.
Establishment of vocational training centre, trained child birth and per-natal care
attendants and women organization were also termed as pressing needs by the
women by that area.
The induction of outside labor may create social and gender issues due to their
unawareness of local customs and norms. It will also cause hindrance to the
mobility of local women.
All the women consulted gave very good comments about the project. They said that
they were in favor of this project. They hope that development will come into their
villages due to this project; their idle youth will get labor work. They would get some sort
of work in that Industrial Park. They said that they were in a very poor condition; and
hoped that this project would bring a ray of hope and prosperity in their lives.
8.5.4   Cultural Values
Cultural attitudes will change as a result of this project and better income, education, and
health are universally desire by every one. People of the area will be having substantial
benefits. The cultural values relating to marriage, suggest that it is the responsibility of
the parents to arrange the marriage of their children. In most of the cases, the father of
bride receives an amount of Afghanis 1-2 lacs equivalent 2000 - 4000 US $ from the
groom or his father.
People of the area have the tradition of cooperating with each other. In case of conflicts,
the community tries to mediate by involving senior wiser person and common friends of
the parties.
On the whole, the local culture has provided lower status to women as compared to
men. This is reflected in placing little value to the education of females, giving little role in
decision making particularly with regard to the issues that relate to their life.

8.6   Women Participation
Women participation is necessary in the development of any country. But here
unfortunately, they always have been restricted only to household work although they
are equally competent and hard working as men.
Women in the project as well as Study Area are mostly housewives and have no
education. But by little training, they will be as useful as men. So, it is hoped that women
should be given employment opportunity during the construction and operation stage of
the Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park.
8.7   Archaeological, Historical and Religious Sites
The proposed Industrial Park is located within the Rodat district near Kabul camp at
Hissar-e-Shahi Camp. The camp was formed by the Government of Afghanistan
keeping in view the plain land availability, its proximity with Nangarhar canal and its
location over Torkham-Jalalabad road. The camp is about 25 km from Jalalabad.
Camp was established in 1999 and since then it is in use by Afghan refugees returning
back from Pakistan. It was planned that Kabul camp will be used as a temporary stay by
these immigrants but the people started to settling here gradually. Today, Hissar-e-Shahi
camp is almost abandoned and Kabul camp has taken its place which is adjacent to
Hissar-e-Shahi camp. Since the area was established about seven (7) years back hence
it has no place of archaeological significance except one grave yard which is about 50 to
70 years old far away from the proposed Industrial Park. No religious and historical site
like mosques, shrines, temples, etc. were observed in the project as well as in the study
area.
8.8   Resettlement Issues
In the Project Area, which will be directly affected by the construction of Industrial Park,
about 21 households will have to be relocated. There is no infrastructure, like electricity,
road, telephone, water supply and sewerage in the Project Area. All houses are made of
tents except one mud house. According to information gathered from project affectees
and other stakeholders of the area, they are illegal occupants on Government Land.

8.9   Evaluation of Assets
The site for the Industrial Park in Jalalabad has been selected at the location of now
abandoned Kabul Camp along Jalalabad-Torkham Highway. The area comprises of
barren land without any bushes or trees and is owned by the Canal Department of
Nangarhar Province.
Preliminary survey determined that there were about 250 mud houses, a petrol pump, a
plastic factory and a large compound of cemented residences on the land that could be
made available by the Government of Afghanistan for the Project. However, the
proposed Industrial Park at Hissar-e-Shahi - Jalalabad has been delimited and carved
out in such a way so as to cause minimum disturbance to the population. Resultantly
only 21 affectees now reside in the area in their Hutments/tents including only one mud
house.
The permanent and semi permanent structures mentioned above will not be disturbed by
the Industrial Park. However, the affected structures have been discussed now:
8.9.1   Permanent Structures
Only three permanent structures constructed of burnt brick masonry walls in cement
mortar and precast concrete roofs exist on the proposed area. They were constructed for
the Administration of the Kabul Camp but are now abandoned with the doors and
windows and to a large extent, the precast concrete roof element removed away. These
have to be demolished but no compensation will be required to be paid.
There is a possibility that during the project construction, the contractor or the client may
rehabilitate the structure for their use and dismantle at the end without any cost to the
client.
8.9.2   Mud Walls
The site is cluttered with mud wall remains of the refugee camp. They carry no value or
use. They can be bulldozed away and levelled under the project construction item of site
clearing.
8.9.3   Occupied Shelters
Over a very small area at the South-West end of the proposed area, 21-families have set
up 20 temporary shelters of plastic/tarpaulin/tree branches etc over the remnant mud
walls of the refugees camp. Sufficient adjacent government land is available to relocate
these families, without affecting their quality of life. However, some compensation is
essentially needed to be paid to them.
8.10  Valuation
The existing shelters shall be removed and reused whereas mud shall be prepared and
used for constructing the new walls at the new locations. All the existing structures have
been valuated and detailed in table below:

8.12  Indigenous People and Women Headed Households
During the social field survey of the project, efforts were made to identify the indigenous
and women headed households along the Project corridor, no such group of people was
identified which comes under the definition of "Indigenous People" as per W.B. O.D.
4.20. Similarly no women headed household was identified in the Project corridor.
8.13  Resettlement Measures
There are 21 families residing within the project area. These immigrants returning from
Pakistan need to be resettled to the nearby areas prior to the start of construction
activities. This impact of resettlement will be of Major nature and will have long terms
impacts on the life of these resettlers. However, from project perspective this impact will
be termed as Major with short term impacts.
8-19



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
AISA has already negotiated with project Affectees and they had agreed for relocation, if
they are paid compensation of $ 200/-and alternate land is provided. AISA decided to
give US$ 200 as compensation per family and to settle them on available adjacent state
land. Affectees of the area were satisfied on this offer.
8.14  Compatibility of Negotiation with Op. 4.12
As per WB OP 4.12 under the heading of eligibility for benefits following steps should be
taken upon:
* Identification of the need of involuntary resettlement:
. A detailed focus census survey should be carried out
. Displaced persons should be consulted for various options for resettlement
* Provided with prompt and effective compensation at full replacement cost
Under OP 4.12, 15 Criteria for eligibility of the exiting group of people under (c ) those
who have no recognizable legal right or claim to land they are occupying. Such affectees
should be provided with compensation for land as well as the assets compensation.
This compensation should be negotiated with the affectees by consultation with them in
the presence of organizations and NGO's in order to make the negotiation process
transparent and protect the rights of the affectees.
Prior to the compensation package agreement between AISA and affectees. Detailed
focus census survey of the affectees was carried out along with the scoping session in
which their views and any clarification about the project as well as their rights were
carried out by the consultants. Hence affectees were made well aware of their rights and
details of the project.
Upon identification of resettlement issues, in a spirit to resolve the issue quickly and
effectively. AISA started negotiation with the affectees in the presence of the
representatives from Ministry of Agriculture, Refugee Camp Organization, Nangarhar
Valley Development Authority, Geodesy and Cartography Department and Government
Judiciary Department. The involvement of these departments ensured that the
negotiation with affectees were neutral and transparent without any pressure.
Three major meeting were held and various options were discussed with the Affectees.
In the end the resettlers were provided with alternate Government land near the site
along with assets compensation of US $ 200/- per family as demanded by the affectees.
Based on the process followed and review of compensation paid it is concluded that as a
first compensation this package has been successfully delivered as they are fully
satisfied. However, it is suggested that further assistance should be provided by AISA
during the resettlement and operational stage of the project.
The affectees' do not have any means of livelihood or land associated with the Project
Area, hence further assistance should be provided to them so that these persons can
become useful members of the society.
8.15  Verification of Resettlement
NESPAK team visited the site on the September 06, 2006 to verify that the Affectees
have evacuated the site or not. It was revealed that all the Affectees have shifted from
the site. The compensation of US $ 200/- have been received by each affectee. The

8.16  Public Consultation and Scoping Sessions
Public participation and support, which is based on the awareness about the objectives
of the project, is one of the critical issues for its success. Several consultations had been
carried out with stakeholders during the field visits.
The objectives of stakeholder consultation were to improve the quality and relevance of
the EIA process, and to contribute to the openness, transparency and dialogue in the
preparation of the report. Special efforts were made to ensure that communication with
the public be efficient and well balanced. The main stakeholder groups were identified
during the phase of the assessment, and additional groups were also invited to
participate in the assessment.
A series of scoping sessions and focus group discussions were carried out at various
locations of the Project and Study Area, i.e. Kabul Camp, Chora Gali and Hissar-e-Shahi
Camp. Table 8-15, given details of scoping sessions and focus group discussions.
Following social and cultural aspects were discussed.
a  Who are the people who might be affected by the project? (Number and size of
* Who are the people likely to be affected by the project? (Number and size of
families, dwellings and villages).
I  What are the main social group structures (communities, classes, castes, tribes,
clans etc.) through which the people organize?
.  What are the authority structures of the groups? Is the authority based on
kinship, seniority, consensus, or democratic voting?
* Are there sacred sites or important archeological or historical sites that might be
affected by the project?
* Which of these groups are aware of the proposed project and of any problems
that might be associated with it?
I  What proportion of the affected community can read or write? Do they have
access to radios, newspapers, or other media? Do they speak the national
language?
*  What NGO's are already in direct contact with the affected people and what is
the nature of their relationship? Are the NGO's strong enough to be effective?
. Which of the groups are responsible for access to or management of
environmental resources etc.

EIA Report
8.16.1  Pressing Needs
After the analysis and assessment of the pressing needs or concerns shown by the local
community during public consultations/scoping sessions, following are the basic
requirements of the Study Area people which should be looked into:
*  Availability of Pure Drinking Water
*  Employment Opportunities During the Construction and Operational phase of the
project
*  Hospital and Medical Facilities
*  High School
*  Metalled Access Roads
These are the genuine needs of the locals of the Study Area which should be resolved.
8.17  Anticipated Socio-economic Impacts
8.17.1  Construction Stage
Socio-economic analysis, for assessment of the impacts of the project on people and
communities in the vicinity, is necessary. During construction stage employment
opportunities would increase which may result in the increased per capita income and
many other facilities such as business opportunities. During the field investigations some
of the locals expressed that there was no significant impacts except one or two on socio-
economic conditions in the area. However there are some impacts worth mentioning as
observed and are stated hereunder:-
During the construction period, the local workers will get opportunity to work on semi-
skilled and labour work jobs, hence they will get experience of construction works, thus
human resource will be developed at local level for future development activities. The
project will greatly affect the life-style of the people. Local people will find themselves in
a new hope of prosperity. The project will have major effects on local economy,
employment and income. These will mainly be positive impacts. Such activities will bring
more business in the Project Area hence boosting its economy. The income level of the
local residents is surely going to increase providing relief to the local residents.
8.17.2  Operational Stage
Socio-economic analysis for the impact assessment is more important in the operational
stage of the proposed project because these impacts will be for a long term.
After the construction of the project, the business potential will increase in the area.
Many of the local technical/non technical workers will be hired during operational stage,
while others will have a chance to engage on similar projects in nearby places. The
increased demand of food grain, vegetables, meat, poultry and other food products will
provide incentive to local farmers to enhance their farm output. So direct and indirect
benefits will be available to local people through increased activity as a result of this
project.
Health facilities will need a big boost in the post project era to cater for the increased
population needs. It is expected that with the general development of the Project Area,
8-26



1-4issar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                          AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
the need for educational facilities will increase manifolds which could be met from
improved resources generated from the proposed project.
Negative impacts anticipated during the operational stage will be the air pollution; noise
and vibrations due to working of machinery which will disturb the local population area
especially during night time.
8.18  Remedial & Mitigation Measures
8.18.1  Construction Stage
In order to use the local labor, it is essential to appoint a Social Development Officer
in the Project Area, because 90% people of the project as well as Study Area are
90% illiterate. Their main source of income or their main occupation is labor work,
hence there is a great need of a Technician who guides and educates them about
the construction methods and use of constructional equipment.
U  Round the clock Health facilities should be provided to the people. A clinic, Basic
Health Unit, or at least a dispensary should be opened as there is no health
facility in the Project Area and people have to travel to Jalalabad City for
treatment.
* A vocational/Technical Education Centre should be opened. At present there is
only one primary school in the Study Area for both boys and girls.
* Social Development is as important as economic development and for social
development these ingredients are necessary.
o  Education
o Health
o Pure Drinking Water, etc.
U  Appointment of a Social Development Officer will be a great help in this regard
. Agreement with the Contractor should be in local language or at least
understandable to the community.
 The Contractor should preferably use the local skilled and un-skilled labor as the
migrant labor may create some social problems. Employment of locals will be an
added benefit to the community.
*  Project facilities should be located at a minimum distance of 500 m from the
existing settlements and built-up areas in order to avoid disturbance to local
community especially women and children.
*  Pure drinking water was the foremost demand of the Project as well as Study
Area people. A Water Filter Plant be installed.
Since the project route is passing through the villages, women activities in the field may
become limited due to the construction activities.
The induction of outside labor may create social and gender issues due to their
unawareness of local customs and norms. It will also cause hindrance to the mobility of
local women.
8-27



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
8.18.2 Operational Stage
In order to minimize the socio-economic impacts during the operational stage, it is
equally necessary to involve the local labor in the operation of different factories.
. As operation stage will be long termed local labor can get more economic
advantages. Skilled labor will be preferred during this stage.
*  In this stage, women of the project as well as the Study Area should be given a
chance to indulge in different kind of activities. Sewing & Embroidery centers and
other technical centers should be opened for the women of the Project Area.
* The need of a Social Development Officer is also essential during the operation
stage. With the involvement of women appointment of a Lady Social
Development Officer and Female Para-medic workers is also required.
Efforts should be made to improve the economic conditions of the people living in the
surrounding areas, by providing them jobs in the industrial units and educated young
men of the area, should be imparted technical training in the institutes set up by various
NGOs, in the nearby city Jalalabad.
. It is necessary to provide job opportunities to the project affectees during
construction and the operation stage of the project by giving them training.
8.19  Outline of Social Management Plan (SMP)
8.19.1  Introduction
Based on the socio-economic conditions of the area, it is imperative to prepare a Social
Management Plan (SMP) for the study area. The outline of the social management plan
is as under:
8.19.2  Health Facilities
As referred earlier under socio-economic condition of the selected area, accessibility to
existent health facilities like hospital, basic health units, dispensary, etc. is virtually non-
and people have to visit the Jalalabad City for emergencies as well as for routine
medical care, etc. In addition to the social and economic hardships that plague women's
lives, women also face great hardship in all other facets of everyday life, including health
care. The current state of health at both the sites ranks among the poorest. The
infrastructure of health care facilities is in ruins as a result of the longstanding political
upheaval, and present facilities lack the equipment and technology necessary to provide
adequate health care. The severe shortage of health facilities exacerbates the incidents
of maternal and infant mortality and both infants and mothers die from treatable diseases
at a high rate simply because of the lack of resources available for treatment.
In the light of above, main emphasize of the social management plan will be to assess
the  existing  health  facilities  and  to  provide  recommendations  for their
provision/improvement. Recommendations will cover the following items but not be
limited.
* Availability/improvement of health facilities.
* Training for professional family planning services.
*  Serious attention to feeding mothers and children and treatment of malnutrition,
8-28



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
anemia, diet deficiency etc.
. Supporting general health literacy among women through lady health workers,
media and films.
*  Provision of medical equipment and adequate supply of medicines.
* Serious controls on importing and use of expired medicines and suporious drugs.
*  Requisite attention and assistance to disabled people.
8.19.3  On Job Training and Training Centers
Since the level of education of the people of both the Hissar-e-Shahi sites is low, hence
it is necessary to provide them on job training facilities during the construction stage so
that they can work properly and can become efficient laborers during construction and
operational stage of the project. SMP will provide recommendations based on the study
to be carried out in the area for on job training or establishment of training centers.
Recommendations may include but not limited only to these ones:
.The people of the project area should be provided on job training which will
enhance their livelihood and skills.
. Training centre should be opened before the operation stage of the project. First
of all, it will educate the people regarding the project and suitably trained labor for
specific industries will be readily available.
. Educate the people about the functions of various inputs being used during the
project
8.19.4  Employment Opportunities
After the analysis of socio-economic data it was concluded that 90% of the local
population is labor. Their socio-economic condition is not so well. They are working in
different kind of factories, petrol pumps and road maintenance already. They are always
in an uncertain condition regarding job due to the uncertain conditions of Afghanistan.
SMP will explore the employment opportunities and give recommendations which may
include:
a  Employment opportunities should be provided on preferential basis to the locals
for both Industrial Parks during the construction as well as the operational stage.
3  As most of the local population of the Industrial Park has an occupation of labor,
hence it is very easy for them to do similar work in projects. However,
streamlining of their skills is needed.
* As the local women are doing household chores, so it is necessary to give them
employment opportunities during the operation stage of the project in specific
industries, they can become useful as earning members of the family.
8.19.5  Technical Education
Analysis of the village profiles and scoping sessions conducted in the project as well as
the study area clearly shows that educational situation facilities available to the local
population are very poor. There are no technical education facilities available to the local
population. SMP will assess the need and resources required for technical education to
make sure that technical manpower for the specific industries should be available before
operational stage of the project. In this regard provision of Vocational Centers should be
sorted out in the project area both for male and female.
8-29



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
8.19.6  Need of Staffing for SMP
The appointment of Social Development Officer and relevant staff is necessary to
prepare a social management plan for the project. The Social Development Officer will
visit the project site regularly along with staff and will carry out the necessary
consultations, interviews with the community, etc. to assess the views of the population
and to assess their demand.
  An office should be set up for the Social Development Officer where the whole
infrastructural facilities e.g. two supportive assistants/staff, peons, computers etc.
should be available to him.
*  In addition to above, the Social Development Officer will also be responsible for
the following tasks:
*  Provide social review of the Project to the concerned environmental staff of AISA.
.  Coordination between Project management and community including NGOs,
CBOs, and other stakeholders.
  Identifying any problems due to the restricted access to the community during
construction.
*  Identifying major issues of conflict between community and the contractor during
the implementation of Project activities.
8.19.7 Terms of Reference (TOR) for Broader Social Assessment
Terms of Reference (TOR) for broader Social Assessment (SA) have been prepared in
relation to the specific industries to be set up. The specific objectives of TOR for (SA)
have been listed below;
* To carry out a social, cultural and political/institutional analysis to identify
potential social impacts of the proposed project due to the implementation.
. To screen social development issues and scope Social Assessment activities for
design and implementation stage specific with each industry.
* To ensure that results of the Social Assessment provide inputs to the monitoring
of project impacts during implementation and the evaluation of project outcomes
at completion.
*To provide inputs to the project design at the detailed design stage including
specific recommendations for preparing social policy framework and training
needs of the locals  specific to each industry.
* Develop a detailed Social Development and Management Plan that includes
comprehensive mitigation measures to ensure that the affected and displaced
persons are appropriately resettled and rehabilitated i.e. to assist them to
improve their livelihoods and standards of living or at least to restore them, in
real terms.
.Assess the current capacity for management of social impacts, develop
institutional arrangements for Hissar-e-Shahi and Kamari Industrial Park Project
and formulate a training and capacity building plan for future. Identification of
specific training needs, measures to promote female employment and strategies
to control child labor etc.
The detail of TOR for broader (SA) has been attached with draft report as Annexure-
Vill.

Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                             AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
CHAPTER 9-CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
9.1   Conclusions
Based on the Master Plan, Preliminary Design, environmental and social field surveys,
and impacts assessment of the proposed Hisari-e- Shahi Industrial Park project, it may
be concluded that although there are some significant negative impacts but would be of
short term during the construction stage. However, there are a few negative impacts that
would be expected during the operational stage but their intensity can be reduced by
taking appropriate measures. The environmental issues related with the Project
Activities are summarized as under:
* Physical impacts like soil erosion, soil contamination, water contamination, air
pollution, high noise level, etc. are of temporary nature during the construction
stage. However, during the operational stage by adopting abatement
technologies such as treatment plants (activated sludge system), air bags,
cyclones, electrostatic precipitators, development of buffer zones and grassy
areas intensity of negative impacts can be minimized. Detailed impacts and
mitigation measures have been discussed in Chapter-5 and Chapter-7.
* During operation stage, disposal of waste will become a problem. Therefore,
proper mitigations have been adopted in the preliminary design including
wastewater treatment plant, safe and environmental friendly disposal of solid
waste and control of gaseous emissions at source. The standards to be followed
both for wastewater treatment and  gaseous emissions have been discussed in
EMMP, Chapter-7.
* The project does not have a single tree. However, there are trees in the Study
Area, which may be cut by the Contractor staff to meet the camp site fire wood
requirements. So, Contractor should use gas cylinders at camp site to fulfill the
fire wood requirements and will ensure that trees should not be cut by the
workers.
. No forest area or wildlife sanctuary exists within the vicinity of the Project Area,
which may be affected by the Project. Few reptiles like lizards and snakes and
few birds like Mynah and house sparrows will be disturbed by the Project
activities and may have to move into nearby areas. This will be a temporary
insignificant impact.
. The project site selected at initial stage was causing the disruption of about 250
temporary residential structures and a plastic factory & petrol pump. Relocation
of these structures was causing a social nuisance. Therefore, project site area
was adjusted in consultation with AISA and finally instead of about 250
households, only 21 households of temporary structures were needed to
relocate. AISA in consultation with other government and non-government
agencies has made payment to the affectees as per their satisfaction.
* There is no issue of acquisition of land as the land was owned by Canal
Department and has been transferred to the AISA.
*Temporary land on lease for establishment of Contractor's camp facilities will be
required and criteria for selection of land and establishment of facilities has been
provided in Chapter -5 and Mitigation Management Matrix(MMM) of Chapter-7,
Table 7.1.
9-1



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                            AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
* No indigenous people and women headed households have been identified in
the Project.
. The other social issues like safety of general public and workers, security
problems, community accessibility issue, women accessibility to fields for their
daily routine life etc. will be of temporary nature and proper mitigations have
been provided in MMM.
.Although no major social issue has been identified during the EIA studies,
howeverthe socioeconomic conditions of the surrounding areas of Hissar-e-
Shahi industrial park are quite adverse in terms of availability of social
infrastructure and facilities. It implies the preparation of a Social Management
Plan (SMP).
*A comprehensive EMMP has been developed identifying the impacts, mitigation
measures, agencies responsible for implementation, monitoring and auditing of
the proposed measures. EMMP also provides the roles and responsibilities of the
agencies responsible for mitigation, monitoring and auditing of EMMP. The
EMMP also provides the  proposed   institutional  setup  for  effective
implementation of the mitigation measures, monitoring parameters, and training
of AISA, NEPA, District Administration, Contractor and Supervisory Consultant
staff, to enhance their capacity. As the EIA Study has been carried out at Master
Planning and Preliminary Design Stage of the Project, so a change management
plan has been provided in the EMMP to cater the changes that may occur at
detailed design and even during construction and operation stages of the Project.
Similarly, generic guidelines for HSE, EMS, Eco-efficiency and Clean Production,
Hazardous Waste Management, Waste Minimization, etc. have also been
provided in EMMP at industrial estate level which will help to prepare detailed
management plans for estate and individual units on later stage by the AISA and
private investors.
. It may be concluded that if proper mitigation measures as given in this report be
implemented, the Industrial Park will cause the least effect on the area's existing
environmental and social setting. On the other hand, it is expected that Project
will generate about 10,000 to 15,000 employment opportunities to the residents
of the area.
9.2   Recommendations
Although comprehensive mitigation measures have been proposed in the report to
minimize the negative impacts and to enhance the positive impacts of the Project,
however, major recommended mitigation measures are summarized as under:
. Soil erosion, water contamination, air pollution and high noise levels should be
controlled  with the use of good engineering practices including land
management, selection of abatement devices, and use of proactive measures,
selection of proper sites, etc. The abatement technologies as mentioned in
Chapter-5 and Chapter 7, Table 7.1 should be adopted especially during the
operational stage of the project.
* It is recommended that a detailed study of groundwater within and nearby vicinity
of project area shall be carried out during detailed Design Stage to assess the
impacts on groundwater quantity due to implementation of the Project. The
proposed groundwater study shall include Electrical Resistively Survey (ERS).
9-2



Hissar-e-Shahi Industrial Park                           AISA / NESPAK
EIA Report
. It is also recommended that a retention pond should be considered within the
proposed storm water network system at detailed design stage.
* Contractor should take due care of the local community and its sensitivity
towards local customs and traditions.
* EMMP proposed in Chapter 7 should be implemented in the true spirit.
a It is also recommended to carry out a detailed Social Assessment Study for the
preparation of Social Management Plan for socioeconomic uplift and proper
management of human resources of surrounding areas.
. In order to address these issues formulation of laws and change in future plans
of the relevant district administration will be required. Therefore, it is suggested
that AISA should coordinate with the relevant district administration of Rodat
District along with the department related with Planning and Development of
Jalalabad at all stages of the project. This will provide awareness of issues to be
dealt by relevant government departments and administration. This coordination
will help relevant authorities to develop or mould their future strategies
proactively to address the anticipated issues likely to arise in the vicinity of the
industrial park.
* It is also recommended that the data/information updated at detailed design
should be incorporated in the report as mechanism  proposed in change
management plan in Chapter 7.
* The findings of the following studies should also be incorporated in the report as
mentioned in change management plan.
o  Eco-Efficiency Study and Cleaner Development Plan which will be
carried out at early in the implementation phase once the facility's
participants will be known. This study will be carried out by an
individual consultant at an approximate cost of US$ 20,000/-.
o  Preparation of detailed EMS as per ISO 14000 for Industrial Park by
the environment specialist to be hired by AISA, based on the
generic guidelines provided in EMMP.
o  Updation of the Hazardous Waste Management framework based
on the periodic review by NEPA to enable the AISA to develop and
incorporate an appropriate strategy to the Waste Management
Plan.
o  In addition, any unforeseen conditions arise at operation stage, or
change in characterization of the effluents, changes may be carried
out in EMMP by the AISA.

REVISED NATIONAL ENVIRONMENTAL
QUALITY STANDARDS (NEQS)
Background
* PEPC in its first meeting held on 10th May 1993 approved the NEQS.
* The approved NEQS were uniform standards applicable to all kind of industrial and
municipal effluent.
* There are 32 parameters prescribing permissible levels of pollutants in liquid effluent
while 16 parameters for gaseous emission.
* In April 1996, the PEPC set up an Environmental Standards Committee (ESC)
headed by Mr. Shams Kasim Lakha to review, inter alia, the NEQS and suggest
changes where necessary, based on conditions in Pakistan.



* The committee realized that some of the parameters were more stringent than other
countries of the region, so the task of the rationalization of NEQS was referred to an
Expert Advisory committee to review and suggest changes, if and where required.
* Before initiating the task, the Expert Committee was expanded to include
representatives of trade and industry.
* The Expert Committee identified ten parameters - eight (8) liquid effluent viz. BOD;
COD; TDS; Chloride; Sulphide; Chromium; Ammonia; and Temperature, and two (2)
gaseous emissions viz. SO2 (Sulphur di oxide) and Oxides of Nitrogen for review.
* After consultation with various organizations the NEQS Expert Advisory Committee
completed its task and proposed it to the ESC.
* Finally after the Environmental Standards Committee endorsed the proposed revised
NEQS, the Pakistan Environmental Protection Council was recommended to approve
the revised draft NEQS.
. In December 28, 1999. PEPC approved the revised NEQS.

Explanations
1. Summing minimum dilution 1:10 on discharge, lower ratio would attract progressively
stringent standards to be determined by the Federal Environmental Protection Agency. By
1:10 dilution means for example, that for each one cubic meter of treated effluent the
recipient water body should have 10 cubic meter of water for dilution of this effluent.
2. Modified Benzene Alkyl Sulphate; assuming surfactant as bio-degradable.
3. Pesticides herbicides, fungicides, and insecticides.
4. Subject to total toxic metal discharge as at S. No.25
5. Applicable only when and where sewage treatment is operational and BOD5=80 mg/I. is
achieved by the sewer treatment system.
6. Provided discharge is not at shore and not within 10 miles of mangrove or other important
estuaries
* The effluent should not result in temperature increase of more than 3C at the edge of the
zone where initial mixing and dilution take place in the receiving water body. In case zone
is not defined, use 100 meters from the point of discharge.
** The value for industry is 200 mg/I.
Note: Dilution of gaseous emissions and liquid effluents to bring them to the NEQS limiting
value is not permissible through excess air mixing blowing in to the gaseous
emissions or through fresh water mixing with the effluent before discharge into
environment.

Explanations:
1. Based on the assumption that the size of the particles is 10 microns or more.
2. Any source.
3. Based on 1% sulphure content in fuel oil. Higher content of sulphure will cause standards to be pro-rated.
4. In respect of emissions of sulphure dioxide and nitrogen oxides, the power plants operating on oil or coal as fuel shall, in addition to National
Environmental Quality Standards (NEQS) specified above, comply with the following standards.

ESTABLISHMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL LABORATORY BY NEPA
Establishment of Environmental Laboratory BY NEPA is recommended keeping in view
the requirement of environmental testing to be carried out in future for subject project as
well as anticipated other projects. This laboratory will be established at NEPA
headquarter in Kabul. The following laboratory staff can handle the EMP activities:
Table - 1: Suggested Laboratory Staff
Sr.                               Nos.
#    Position    Education        Required   Details                -   --

Ii
Laboratory  Bachelor     of 1
2    Technician  Science
3     Helpers   Metric           3
Note: The above staff shall get three months training program in Pakistan in
Environmental Laboratory Techniques.
